British Empire Defense

Sir Hankey, in the Name of the Cabinet Secretary

Visits Various Autonomous Territories for Negotiations

(London) Sir Hankey, a member of the Imperial Defence Committee, will set out on Friday to visit various autonomous territories to discuss imperial defence issues. Sir Hankey recently stated, "I will discuss everything with the governments of South Africa, Australia, New Zealand, and Canada in the name of the Cabinet Secretary and the Secretary of the Imperial Defence Committee." The purpose of Sir Hankey's trip is very broad. He has not received specific instructions or been assigned specific tasks. The emphasis is on discussing various issues, including economics, finance, commerce, military affairs, and strategy, with politicians in the autonomous territories, seeking their opinions, and informing them of the views of the British government. Of particular importance are the Ottawa Agreement and the issue of Imperial Defence. Regarding the Ottawa Agreement, some provisions have not been implemented by the autonomous territories or have not been fully implemented. Regarding Imperial Defence, the issue of protecting the Imperial sea lanes and naval bases in the Far East will inevitably be discussed. (Havas, 8th)

Konoe's Opinion Letter

Criticism from the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs

(Tokyo) Although the Ministry of Foreign Affairs avoids formal discussions on Prince Konoe's opinion letter on the United States, a summary of criticisms from various departments within the ministry is as follows: (1) The opinion letter generally presents the current state of Japan-U.S. relations and the U.S. attitude toward Japan based on facts. In particular, regarding the Manchurian problem, it clearly indicates that although the U.S. broadly recognizes the reality, it still adheres to its principles and policies, intending to continue its non-recognition doctrine. This shows that there is still a considerable distance between Japan and the U.S. in their understanding of the situation in the Far East, which is noteworthy. (2) The U.S. suspects the limits of Japan's policy towards China. The U.S. believes that Japan's demand to abolish the 5-5-3 naval ratio is related to its Far East policy and feels a sense of danger, which proves this point. (3) The current relationship between Japan and the U.S. is extremely peaceful. At the beginning of this year, when Hirota and Hull exchanged official documents, both sides unanimously asserted that the problems between Japan and the U.S. could be resolved through negotiation. However, the U.S. still harbors suspicion and anxiety, feeling uneasy about Japan's actions. Therefore, to fundamentally establish peace between Japan and the U.S., it is essential for the U.S. to abandon these feelings of suspicion. Regarding this point, Prince Konoe's opinion letter seems too polite in enlightening the U.S., leaving something to be desired. Although Prince Konoe implies that Japan needs to clearly express the new principles of Far Eastern peace to the U.S., Japan's actions from the outbreak of the Manchurian Incident to the Amau Statement have already clearly expressed these principles. Now, if Japan wants to propose its principles anew, how will it do so? This reveals that the central problem of future diplomacy with the U.S. still lies ahead, and Prince Konoe's opinion letter seems to lack a progressive spirit in this regard. (4) The opinion letter is generally appropriate and solid, fully demonstrating the spirit of peace of the Japanese government and people toward the U.S., which should not be overlooked. (Dentsu, 8th)

(Tokyo) Army Minister Hayashi, who met with Prince Konoe yesterday to listen in detail to the situation in the United States, told reporters that he only listened to Prince Konoe's observations about the United States and did not discuss future policies toward the U.S. Prince Konoe said that misunderstandings about Japan are still deep among the American government and people, so efforts should be made in the future to eliminate these misunderstandings and make the U.S. fully understand Japan and the Orient. I deeply agree with this, he said. (Dentsu, 8th)

Japan Will Establish

Information Library in New York

Konoe Made This Suggestion Upon His Return

(Nanjing) In the opinion letter on the U.S. issue submitted by Prince Konoe, he mentioned the establishment of a new information library in New York. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs greatly supports this proposal. This type of library was first established by the United Kingdom in 1920 and has been quite effective ever since. Japan now feels the need to emulate it for the sake of promoting friendship with the U.S. The United Kingdom uses this library as the de facto representative office of its government for its political, economic, and social policies towards the U.S. The maintenance costs for the library are set at 50,000 yuan per year, and it has achieved practical results in its work with the U.S. The authorities of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs, in light of these actual circumstances, stipulated last year that the creation costs for the information library, a new project for diplomatic work, would be 100,000 yuan and the maintenance costs would be 80,000 yuan. It has already been decided by the ministry's council, and efforts are being made to establish it this year. Prince Konoe's report upon returning from his visit to the U.S. also expressed the same opinion, which is even more helpful. Therefore, they want to expedite its realization and also plan to build a similar library in Baghdad, the center of Europe. (United Press, 8th)

Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs

Reform Plan for Manchurian Organizations

Inconsistent with the Military's Plan

(Tokyo) Regarding the reform of organizations in Manchuria, the plan of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the plan of the Army are quite different. Although the basic principles are the same in both plans, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs advocates clearly defining the division between military, diplomatic, and administrative affairs in Manchuria and absolutely opposes the establishment of a colonial administrative organization, such as the Governor-General in Korea in the past. The contents of the plan of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs are as follows: (1) Abolish the Governor-General of Kwantung, establish a new state governor, and preserve the two-in-one system of the Ambassador to Manchuria and the Commander of the Kwantung Army. However, retain the Minister of Colonial Affairs' supervisory authority over the South Manchuria Railway. (2) Gradually make the Ambassador to Manchuria a purely diplomatic official under the supervision of the Minister of Foreign Affairs. (3) Reform the authority of the Commander of the Kwantung Army. Although discretion is delegated to the Army, it should be separated from the duties of the Ambassador in the future and only govern military administration and command. (4) Gradually improve all judicial, administrative, and economic powers of the Ambassador Plenipotentiary and all administrative powers transferred by the Governor-General of Kwantung to adapt to the current state of "Manchukuo." (5) The state governor is supervised by the Minister of Colonial Affairs. (6) In order to realize the economic control of Japan and Manchuria, a joint committee should be established under the direction of each minister to study concrete plans for economic prosperity. (Dentsu, 8th)

Daring Feat by Canadian Aviators

Attempting Non-Stop Long-Distance Flight

Aiming to Break French Record

Toronto At 5:12 AM this morning, Canadian aviators Captain Reed and Captain Alling took off together in an aircraft, planning to fly directly to Baghdad to break the world's non-stop long-distance flight record held by Lieutenants Rossi and Codouce. The aircraft they are using is named Seafarer, the same aircraft that the famous British aviators Mr. and Mrs. Morrison flew across the Atlantic last year. Mr. and Mrs. Morrison departed from Wales, UK on July 23 last year, planning to fly to New York, but were forced to land in a field in Stratford, Connecticut at night due to fog and dwindling fuel. The aircraft body was severely damaged and later fully repaired. Rossi and Codouce are French aviators who also flew from New York in May last year, also attempting to fly directly to Baghdad, but were forced to land in Rayak, Syria due to a leak in the fuel tank, covering 5,653 and a half miles. U.S. Treasury Orders 150 Million Yuan of Gold

Transferred from San Francisco to Denver

Rumors of Preparing for War in the Pacific

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau today confirmed that the Treasury Department will order the transfer of gold worth 150 million yuan from San Francisco to Denver. Senior Treasury officials refused any discussion and would not answer whether this move was related to Japan. According to rumors circulating in financial circles here and in New York, this transfer is due to the possibility of war in the Pacific, so the Treasury Department believes that the interior is safer. San Francisco Outside rumors that the Mint here will transfer a huge amount of gold to Denver due to fears of earthquakes. People in San Francisco just laughed at this. Thirty years ago, the city of San Francisco was destroyed by fire, and residents still do not believe that it was due to an earthquake. Therefore, they do not pay any attention to the reason for the transfer of gold given by Treasury Secretary Morgenthau from Washington. However, they say that the Mint here will be demolished soon, so the gold is temporarily transferred to Denver in preparation for the reconstruction of a new building. As for the rumors circulating outside that this move is related to the war in the Pacific, no one in San Francisco is willing to express any opinion. (National News, 7th)

Denver Officials at the Denver Mint today declined to comment on the Treasury Department's plan to move a huge amount of gold from the San Francisco Mint to here, but said that everything is under the control of Washington and that they only know that they will receive a batch of cash. Only Holds the Position of Ordinary Ambassador

Vienna The issue of Papen's ambassadorship to Austria has been considered by the Austrian government for a long time. The final resolution has been reached. Rome Three sisters of Archduke Otto of the old Austrian Habsburg royal family are now staying at the villa of Prince Bourbon Parma, a relative. Austrian Prime Minister Continues Previous Policy

Dollfuss' Spirit Lives On

(Paris) Austrian Chancellor Schuschnigg recently gave a speech in French, "narrating the circumstances of former Chancellor Dollfuss's murder." The recording of the speech was preserved, and the French National Radio Station broadcast Schuschnigg's speech again today. Schuschnigg "detailed the circumstances of Dollfuss's murder, saying that for two years the former Chancellor struggled hard and persevered, with the intention of preserving Austria's independence and dignity. Unexpectedly, villains attacked Austria repeatedly, and stopped at nothing to achieve their goals. Austria is an old civilized country of thousands of years, from which Germanic and Christian culture all originated, and it is the source of thought for the whole of Europe. Dollfuss loved it, but external forces destroyed it, which is truly heartbreaking." Schuschnigg continued, "The policy pursued by Dollfuss was a policy of maintaining peace. Although Dollfuss is dead, his policy must continue. In short, the purpose we hold is to resist violence with law, to resist evil with justice, and to resist madness with reason. Only the world can understand this sentiment." (Havas, 7th)

Vienna German radio stations began anti-Austrian propaganda again yesterday. Hindenburg

A Touching Scene at the Funeral

The Coffin Placed in the Tower on the Fourteenth Day

Citizens from Afar Reverently Pay Their Respects

All Attendees Wear Formal Attire

A Dazzling Array of Colors

One of the most solemn and touching scenes of the state funeral for the German national hero, Hindenburg, in Tannenberg, unfolded this afternoon. After Chancellor Hitler recited the eulogy, eight officers stepped forward and lifted Hindenburg's remains from the catafalque. Amidst a booming 101-gun salute, the remains were placed in the "General's Tower," where they will remain for fourteen days, allowing people from all over the country to come and pay their respects. As the eight officers slowly carried the coffin towards the General's Tower, the military band played the march of the Third Guard Regiment, which Hindenburg had commanded during his lifetime. After Hindenburg's coffin was placed in the tower, Hindenburg's family, Chancellor Hitler, Field Marshal Mackensen, and Minister of Defense General von Blomberg entered to pay their silent respects before the coffin. Then, the honor guard and those attending the funeral filed in to pay their last respects to the late president. It is estimated that over 20,000 people participated in the ceremony. However, the enclosure within the walls of the Tannenberg memorial could only accommodate 4,000 people. The remaining crowd had to stand outside the walls or gather at the nearby Hindenburg Sports Field, where a radio broadcast of the entire funeral proceedings allowed them to listen as if they were present. Those standing within the walls included important government officials, former imperial army officers, key figures from the current national defense forces and navy, special envoys from various countries, and representatives from major cities, churches, and organizations in Germany, as well as commanders of the stormtroopers. The space was packed with people. All civilians attending the funeral wore formal attire, creating a magnificent spectacle alongside the colorful uniforms of the army and navy officers and the gold-trimmed formal attire of the diplomats. The most eye-catching figures included British General Hamilton in his Scottish red military uniform, an Austrian officer in his green military uniform, the Egyptian envoy with his blood-red tassel on his embroidered hat, the Chinese diplomats in their gold-embroidered formal attire, and the Hungarian envoy in his ancient nobleman's attire. (National Telegram, 7th)

The Hero's Hometown Flies Flags at Half-Mast to Mourn

Poznań, now part of Polish territory after the war, originally belonged to Germany and was known as Posen. It is Hindenburg's hometown. Hindenburg was born there in 1847, his father being a Prussian officer. The city did not pay much attention to the passing of President Hindenburg. However, today, during Hindenburg's burial, the city's military barracks flew flags at half-mast to mourn. The German consulate was closed because its staff went to Tannenberg to participate in the funeral. German-owned shops and factories allowed their employees and workers to listen to the broadcast of the funeral service. The dilapidated area where Hindenburg's family had lived for generations has seen a continuous stream of visitors paying their respects after his death. However, although Hindenburg's former residence still stands, few people know that it is the birthplace of a great European hero and statesman. (National Telegram, 8th)

Why is the Greek Prime Minister Visiting Germany?

Greek Prime Minister Tsaldaris is currently in Bad Reichenhall, Germany. The Greek Minister of the Army, Kondylis, and the Chief of Staff, Gassanis, will also be going to Germany for vacation. There is much speculation about the continuous arrival of Greek dignitaries in Germany. (National Telegram, 8th)

Roosevelt

Inspecting the Drought-Stricken Areas

Twenty-Four States Affected by Disaster

Losses Amount to 1.5 Billion

President Roosevelt spoke to 10,000 farmers at Lake Texwell, urging them to maintain their faith and courage to fight against this year's unprecedented drought. The government will also do its best to provide relief. Although the audience looked wan, they welcomed the president enthusiastically. After the speech, they cheered in approval. Some farmers held up large banners with the words, "You have given us wine, please give us water." Upon seeing this, the president replied that wine is made by human effort, while water is determined by heaven. Therefore, the difficulty of the two cannot be compared. However, the government is doing its best to engage in public works and water storage projects, and several projects are already under construction. From there, the president will travel to Minneapolis and Rochester. After arriving in Rochester, he will give another national radio address, likely on the topic of the drought. (National Telegram, 7th)

(Washington) Assistant Director of the Central Relief Bureau, Weissbrodt, reported to President Roosevelt today about the severity of the drought in the country, stating that 26 million people have been affected. 400,000 households in 24 American states are currently receiving government assistance. Millions of livestock have died, with estimated losses reaching 1.5 billion yuan. This is the most serious disaster the Relief Bureau has ever encountered. Since Congress adjourned in mid-June, the drought has increased fourfold. Over 60% of the country's agricultural areas are now classified as disaster areas by officials. According to opinions, at least one-tenth of the affected households need to relocate to other parts of the United States in the hope of regaining economic independence. The Central Emergency Relief Bureau is urgently organizing relief agencies in 20 states to assist disaster-stricken farmers in relocating. The Federal Land Bank is currently providing loans to help farmers. The estimated number of cattle deaths in the disaster area is between 7 million and 10 million. President Roosevelt delivered a speech to farmers today on the side of the road during his return trip to Washington. The car was air-conditioned, but the heat wave outside was unbearable, with the temperature reaching 113 degrees Fahrenheit in the shade. (Reuters, 8th)

The Heat Wave in the Southwestern United States Has Not Subsided

Chicago's southwest is experiencing another heatwave, with temperatures rising above 100 degrees Fahrenheit in a wide area. Phillipsburg, Kansas, reached 117 degrees Fahrenheit. There has been light rain in some of the disaster area, but it is a drop in the bucket. People, livestock, and crops continue to suffer. Kansas is particularly hard hit. The governor today requested that the state's railways transport water free of charge to the worst-hit areas. The disaster situation is also severe in other parts of the West and Midwest. The temperature in Kansas City yesterday was 110 degrees Fahrenheit. Grain prices in Chicago are soaring due to the drought. Prices for wheat, rye, and barley today broke the season's records, while corn prices are the highest they have been in recent years. (National Telegram, 7th)

A 300-Year-Old Ancient Palace

The Governor-General's Residence in Northern Ireland Destroyed by Fire

Important Documents Saved, Cause of Fire Unknown

William III Once Commanded Battles Here

(London) Hillsborough Castle, the Governor-General's residence in Northern Ireland, built 300 years ago and located near the capital of Northern Ireland, was destroyed by a fire today. Staff, residents, police, and the Belfast fire brigade extinguished the fire after four hours, but only one-third of the building remained intact, and even that suffered minor damage. The Governor-General was not in the residence at the time, and the Governor-General's secretary was also on leave. The fire started in the secretary's office and spread to the entire building. The head of the Governor-General's guard, in honor of President Hindenburg's funeral, raised a flag to half-mast on the roof and suddenly saw flames erupting, so he immediately called the police. By the time the Belfast fire brigade arrived, after racing 12 miles, the fire had already broken through the roof and spread elsewhere. At the same time, the Governor-General's staff, police, and villagers rushed to move valuable documents, paintings, utensils, and artworks from the residence. They were lowered from the windows and piled onto the lawn, where police guarded them. The fire spread rapidly, and within an hour, the roof collapsed, and the magnificent ballroom and other rooms were reduced to ashes. A total of 30 rooms were destroyed. The rooms where the Prince of Wales and the Prince had recently resided were also completely destroyed. Hillsborough Castle was purchased by the British government and handed over to the Northern Irish government to be used as the Governor-General's residence. William III resided here in 1690 to command the Irish war. The cause of the fire is unknown, but it is believed to be accidental. The residence may be rebuilt in the future. (Reuters, 7th)

Hubei Province Experiences Combined Flooding and Drought

Zhang Qun Asks the Central Government for Subsidies

(Hankou) Zhang Qun arrived at the Central Executive Yuan on the 8th, saying that Hubei is suffering from both floods and droughts, and the people's livelihood is devastated. Although the droughts of the 16th and 17th years of the Republic and the floods of the 15th and 20th years of the Republic were severe, there have rarely been simultaneous floods and droughts like this year. The current disaster area is expanding, and the society is increasingly panicked. Water conservancy is neglected, agricultural administration is dysfunctional, and human planning is lacking. The responsibility cannot be shirked. The provincial government, learning from past mistakes, believes that fundamental disaster preparedness is urgent. The measures include: A. Installing water pumps; B. Repairing ponds and weirs; C. Installing siphon pipes; D. Repairing ditches. A total of 2.4 million yuan is needed. He pleaded for consideration for the suffering people and requested subsidies to help realize these measures. He also telegraphed Kong Xiangxi, asking him to find ways to relieve the disaster victims. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Zhang Qun previously sent Nan Kui to Nanjing to report the disaster to the central government and request relief. Ministry of Finance Extends Deadline

(Central News Agency, 8th)

(Hangzhou) A hurricane hit Hangzhou City on the morning of the 8th, with flying sand and rocks and a strong momentum, which had not stopped by 10:00 AM. The temperature dropped. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Chongqing-Kunming Air Route Still Difficult to Implement

(Nanjing) Although the Executive Yuan has resolved to establish the Chongqing-Kunming air route between Chongqing, Sichuan, and Kunming, Yunnan, four aircraft purchased from the United States have not yet arrived, and the required funds of approximately 300,000 yuan still need to be raised. Therefore, it is still difficult to implement for the time being. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Hunan-Based Huai Merchants Guild Petitions

(Nanjing) The Hunan-Based Huai Merchants Guild is petitioning because Chen Rujin of the Hunan Salt Affairs Inspection Branch is oppressing Huai merchants in Hunan, forcing them to pay advance taxes amounting to several million yuan. Recently, he has further forced Huai merchants to depreciate prices and compete for sales, violating the regulations. Chairman Xu Yongli and others petitioned the Ministry of Finance, which ordered the Salt Affairs Office to telegraph Hunan to postpone implementation. However, Chen disobeyed in secret, fabricating facts to intensify pressure in Hunan and sending personnel to the Huai Merchants Guild to interfere with the guild's affairs. Xu Yongli, the standing chairman of the guild, and Huai merchant representatives Yi Yinting, Song Fumei, and Li Zelin, among others, went to the Executive Yuan on the morning of the 8th to petition. Chen Rui, a counselor from the Executive Yuan, met with them and promised to convey the petitioners' requests to President Wang and order the Ministry of Finance to handle them fairly. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

The Diplomatic Community Has Not Received

News of Hong Kong Being Opened as a Tax Port

(Nanjing) According to reports, the British government plans to open Hong Kong as a tax port. According to news from the diplomatic community, this has only been reported in the newspapers, and no such report has been received. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Rice Reserves in Nanjing Dwindling Daily

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Rice Industry Guild and the Rice Shop and Rice Shop Association are asking the competent authorities to find ways to provide relief and are asking the Social Affairs Bureau to borrow funds from the banking community to purchase rice. However, the banking community has consistently refused to grant loans. The supply from out-of-town merchants has decreased, and rice reserves are dwindling daily. Rice prices have recently soared. On the evening of the 7th, a meeting was convened with various rice merchants in Xiaguan and the city center. On the morning of the 8th, five representatives, including Tang Qiyu and Jiang Helong, were sent to the Social Affairs Bureau to appeal again. Section Chief Kuang Yunwen met with them and stated that he would immediately convey their representations. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

(Nanjing) It is reported that the amount of rice reserves surveyed in Nanjing last time has suddenly decreased by about 20,000 dan. If the survey is not wrong, it means that the grain merchants are secretly hoarding to manipulate prices. The Social Affairs Bureau stated that the lack of rice reserves is a matter of great concern to them and that they may be able to find a relief solution in the short term. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the National Private Electricity Industry Association

(Nanjing) The National Private Electricity Industry Association recently held its sixth second meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees in Nanjing, resolving: (1) This year's general meeting will be held in Fuzhou in late October. The date will be announced to all members after a ship is selected. During the meeting, an electrical exhibition will still be held as last year, and a film will be made to commemorate the event. (2) Zhu Chengye will be sent to attend the International Electricity Industry Joint Annual Meeting held in Switzerland. (3) Shen Sifang will be sent to attend the Engineers Association Annual Meeting held in Jinan. Finally, Zhu Qianran reported on the reorganization of the Jiujiang Yinglu Company, and Shen Sifang reported on the reorganization of the Wuhu Mingyuan Company. After the meeting, a dinner was held at the Central Hotel. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

(Nanjing) The South African General Branch presented Chairman Chiang with a silver city and a eulogy. The silver city is eight feet in circumference and about two feet high, extremely exquisite and delicate. The original text of the eulogy reads: "Oh, Chairman Chiang, the pillar of the party and the nation, your great achievements surpass historical records. Receiving the mandate, you swore to lead the army, invincible in all directions. Within two years, you unified the North and the South. Despite the dangers and obstacles, you have not rested. You then led the army to suppress the Communists. Just as your merit was about to be achieved, you encountered the Min rebellion, which occupied the land and claimed the people, acting secretly. Fortunately, relying on your prestige, you wiped out the rebellion and consolidated the foundation of the country. Your reputation has spread overseas, three hundred thousand miles away. We respectfully present this humble tribute, to be admired forever." It is reported that the item has been transferred by the Central Organization Committee to the Military Affairs Committee for safekeeping. (Central News Agency, 8th)

Truth about the Train Collision on the Pinghan Railway

(Beiping) The Seventh and Second mixed train heading north on the Pinghan Railway, which departed from Hankou on the night of the 4th, arrived at Zhujiawan Station south of Xiaogan. Because the Eighth and Eighty-Third freight train was added to the south, the Seventh and Second train stopped outside the station. Unexpectedly, the southbound freight train did not stop after entering the station and drove straight towards the Seventh and Second train on the same track, causing a collision. The locomotives were completely destroyed, and one flagman was seriously injured. The Seventh and Second train suffered less damage because it was stationary at the station, and the passengers were unharmed. Efforts are being made to repair the damaged locomotives. (Special Dispatch, 8th)

International Commercial Telegram

丨Special Commercial Intelligence from Reuters, August 8th丨

Gold and Silver

This morning in London, the price of gold rose by two and a half pence, reaching one hundred thirty-eight shillings and a half pence.

In the London silver market, the United States was the main buyer, and China sold. The market conditions were stable. The spot price was twenty pence nine three seven five, up one two five. Futures were twenty-one pence, up ○ six two five.

Exchange Rates

Although talk of inflation in the U.S. and Britain still exists, the pressure to sell dollars in the London foreign exchange market from the European continent this morning was slightly reduced compared to yesterday. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the U.S. dollar was five dollars six and three seven five cents, the same as the closing rate for the U.S. and British currencies yesterday. At 11:00 AM, it rose by three one two five cents, but it fell by half a cent at noon, to five dollars six and one eight seven five cents. This price remained unchanged until 2:00 PM. One U.S. dollar is equivalent to three shillings eleven and four one four pence in British currency.

The opening exchange rate between Britain and France was seventy-six francs thirty-four, the same as yesterday's price, and remained unchanged until 2:00 PM.

The New York foreign exchange market was stable this morning. The opening exchange rate between the U.S. dollar and the British pound fell by twenty-five cents, to five dollars six and one two five cents. At 10:30 AM, it rose by one two five cents, to five dollars six and two five cents. This is the most recent price.

Securities

Before the opening of the New York stock market, the factors favorable to market conditions were (1) railway freight traffic, reaching approximately six hundred thousand and ninety cars, a number similar to last week's; (2) steel industry news, slightly better than before. The factor unfavorable to market conditions was the drought damage to commerce, a major factor in the current general situation. When the stock market opened today, the trend was stable, but there was little development in the market. Many important securities showed no change. Although the foothold strengthened at the opening, people lacked confidence, and it is expected that prices will not fluctuate much.

Cotton and Wheat

The cotton market in New York was stable this morning. The opening price rose by three points. It continued to rise before noon. The latest price rose by six points compared to the opening price. People in the industry are now awaiting the U.S. Department of Agriculture's report on cotton production. The general opinion is that if the reported numbers are lower than expected, the price of cotton will rise sharply.

The opening price of wheat in New York fell by about one point, partly due to profit-taking. However, some said that the foothold of the cotton market was strong and prices were about to rise.

Liverpool Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market fell slightly due to profit-taking. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was six shillings and two and a half pence, down six two five.

Liverpool Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market opened firm. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was six, nine three, up five points.

Rubber

London Rubber: The opening was strong. At noon, the trading price for October futures was seven pence five six two five, up ○ six two five.

The Western Progress of the Longhai Railway Project

(Xi'an) The track-laying project for the Tongxi section of the Longhai Railway has progressed westward from Weinan and is expected to reach Xi'an by the end of this year. The Ba River Railway is currently being rushed to completion. Due to the large number of culverts, it may be difficult to open to traffic for a while. Currently, a temporary road is being built under the bridge, about one kilometer long, with a gradient of 8 or 9 per thousand, to allow traffic to cross the river as soon as possible. The river bridge is expected to be completed within one month and should be finished in about two weeks. The construction of station buildings west of Weinan is currently being tendered. Yu Jishi Discusses the Bandit Situation on the Zhejiang Border

(Hangzhou) Yu Jishi returned to the province from the Zhejiang border and discussed the bandit suppression situation with reporters: (1) The security regiments opened into eastern Jiangxi and captured Linhujiang, Zhengjiafang, Zhangcun, Tongjiafang, and Zhengjiawan. The remnants of the bandits in Nuanshui Zihukou and Daqiaotou in eastern Jiangxi were gradually wiped out. The bandit forces suffered heavy losses. Government troops are building dams and roads to strictly blockade the area. The bandits have broken up into smaller units and circled from Dexing to Zongru and the Centipede Ridge area, repeatedly attempting to harass Kaihua and Changshan. They were all defeated by dispatched troops. According to confessions from prisoners, they are the 31st Division of the Pseudo-Tenth Army and the Huade Li Independent Battalion, etc. (2) It is reported that the troops of Red Bandits Luo Binghui and Huang Ligui have been scattered by our army and are fleeing to various parts of northern Fujian, which is a chance for us to encircle and annihilate them. We are currently carrying out encirclement and suppression from all sides. (Special dispatch, 8th)

Han and Song Meet in Qingdao

Negotiations on Dredging the Xiaoqing River

Jinan Communication: According to a long-distance phone call from Qingdao on the evening of the 5th, Han Fuqu, Chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, came east from Jinan by special train yesterday (the 4th). Due to slight delays along the way, he stopped overnight at the Jiaozhou Railway Station. This morning (the 5th), he departed from Jiaozhou at 5:00 AM and arrived in Qingdao at 8:00 AM. Ge Guangting, Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, and many others greeted him at Cangkou. Song Ziwen, a member of the National Economic Council, Shen Honglie, Mayor of Qingdao, Peng Dongyuan and Lu Mengxiong, members of the Jiaoji Railway Committee, and leaders of various Qingdao agencies were all waiting to greet him at the station. Accompanying Han were consultants Ge Jinzhang, Han Duofeng, Guo Zhigang, Zhang Liansheng, and many others. After Han got off the train and exchanged brief greetings with those welcoming him, he left the station and took a car to the Qingdao Club to rest.

At 5:00 PM, Han went to Song Ziwen's residence on Fushan Road to meet with Song. They talked for about two hours and had detailed discussions on the matter of dredging the Xiaoqing River. Song stated that although the Economic Council could not fully assume responsibility for the funds for dredging the Xiaoqing River, it would do its best to assist within a possible range. As for the amount of funds, it would be determined after visiting Jinan for inspection. At 6:30 PM, Han and others returned to their private residence. That evening, at 7:00 PM, Shen Honglie and Ge Guangting hosted a banquet for Han and others at the Yingbin Hotel. Song Ziwen and other dignitaries were all present to accompany them. Han and others attended the banquet as scheduled. Dozens of guests and hosts enjoyed themselves until 10:00 PM and then dispersed. Han returned to his private residence to rest. Tomorrow (the 6th) at 7:00 PM, the entire committee of the Jiaoji Railway will host a banquet for Han at Peng Dongyuan's residence. The conversations between Han and Song with visitors are recorded below:

(1) Han Fuqu said, "This time I came to Qingdao purely in response to the telegram from Member Song (Ziwen) and to visit Mayor Shen Honglie and Chairman Ge, and have no other tasks. Member Song previously agreed to go to Jinan, so at the end of last month, I ordered Director Zhang (Honglie) to go to Qingdao to welcome him. At that time, Member Song was unable to set off due to matters and telegraphed back inviting me to come again for a meeting to discuss engineering costs related to dredging the Xiaoqing River and joint transportation with the Yellow River, and requested that the Economic Council allocate funds to assist in the project. Last time I came to Qingdao, I had already talked with Song. Later, Director Zhang came, carrying a report on Shandong's construction over the years and future plans, and presented them to Song. Song then expressed his willingness to assist in the project through the Economic Council, but there were no definite and concrete results. I just met with Member Song at his residence, and we had further discussions on the issues of carrying out the construction of the Xiaoqing River project and the Qingdao-Yellow River joint transportation. Song then agreed to allocate funds to assist in the project, but it must wait until Song inspects the Xiaoqing River project in Jinan before deciding. As for the matter of Qingdao Shandong University's financial assistance, because the current expenses in Shandong are extremely tight, it is really impossible to raise such a large amount of funds. I am also deeply regretful about this and unable to help. In recent days, various parties have repeatedly made requests, and President Wang specially sent Director Li Shengwu to Shandong for this purpose. I heard that Li has now arrived in Jinan and then took the second train to Qingdao last night (the 4th), but I have not yet met with him. In the future, I can only reluctantly take on a part, and wait until I meet Li before talking. I do not intend to stay in Qingdao for long, and will ask Song to return to Jinan with me in two or three days, which should be around the 10th."

(2) Song Ziwen said, "Regarding the Xiaoqing River project, Director Zhang also mentioned this matter when he came to Qingdao a few days ago. Now, I have invited Chairman Han (Fuqu) to come to Qingdao again purely for further concrete discussions. The Economic Council will be able to do its best to assist within a possible range. It is difficult to expect the Economic Council to be fully responsible for these project funds. However, depending on Shandong Province's plans for carrying out the project, it will be able to assist at any time. The result of the discussion with Chairman Han is just that. As for whether I will go to Jinan or not, if there are no important matters to hinder me at that time, I can go west with Chairman Han by the same car to return the kindness of repeated invitations, or I may go alone again. It is still undetermined." (5th)

Page 9

Northwest Inspection Report by Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

Qinghai Province is Rich in Forest Products

On the 24th, departing from Xiangtang, "Shina," five li away, has about forty or fifty households. Beans and wheat are abundant, and rapeseed flowers are more than half a zhang tall. Across the river, one can see the county seat of Minhe County. The houses are sparse, and the market is likely not prosperous. However, the yellow rapeseed flowers, the oily green beans and wheat, the shady trees, and the constant flow of canals make for a pleasant scenery, just like in Jiangnan. The land in the Shina area is commonly called "large paddy fields." Elm and poplar trees are planted above the fields, and fruit trees are also sparsely planted in the fields, with beans, wheat, potatoes, etc. planted underneath, all of which are very fertile. The land is fertile and the water conservancy is excellent compared to other places. Yangjiadian, ten li away, has steep and difficult slopes. The Huang River (such as a tributary of the upper reaches of the Yellow River, coming from Huangyuan County in northeastern Qinghai) on the left of the road has recently seen a sudden decrease in water flow due to a prolonged drought, resulting in many rafts and leather bags being stranded midway. The rocks on the river bank are shiny and bright. When broken, they have toughness, seemingly containing lead, zinc, and other substances. Villages in various counties along the river in Qinghai can mostly use river water to irrigate fields, as if applying fertilizer, as the river water contains mineral salts and sticky soil. The river water flows eastward into Gansu, and the water势 increases. If it can be channeled to irrigate the fields, increase production, and revitalize the rural economy, it can be expected soon.

Lianhuatai, ten li away, has a towering temple tower built on a high ridge with lush trees. People say that the barren mountains of Gansu and Qinghai do not grow trees, which proves that this is purely nonsense. The boundary marker between Minhe and Ledu counties is located below the tower, but unfortunately, the words are blurry and difficult to distinguish. Going further to Zaoshiya, the cliff on the right of the road is steep and towering into the clouds. The abyss on the left of the road is thousands of zhang deep, making it terrifyingly dangerous. Someone has engraved "One Dragon" on the cliff, and the winding and narrow road can be imagined. On the opposite cliff, the four characters "Never Forget National Humiliation" are inscribed, and the dangerous road and worried heart make one feel even more alarmed when reading them. A cliff stretches out, shading the scorching sun. More than a dozen people are sitting under the shade, all of whom are going to Gansu Province to work. After resting and chatting with them, most of them asked anxiously, "Have you seen the flowers being marked (referring to opium poppies) when you came up (from Gansu to Qinghai, commonly referred to as 'coming up'; conversely, it is called 'coming down')?" The answer was, "One-fourth of the area has been marked." They then said, "Oh, that's still early. But I heard that the sales of new opium are sluggish this year, and we who suffer (i.e., work) will also suffer a bit. In previous years, each flower festival could earn twenty or so yuan, but this year it's impossible, right?" Another worker said, "A'san came back sick the day before yesterday and said that his old customers from previous years are all marking the flowers themselves this year, and even the pampered eldest daughter (referring to his daughter) in his family is showing her snow-white skin under the fire-like heat (a common term for the sun) and marking the flowers." Another person said, "In that case, we are going to starve." The words they said mostly contained practical information about the rural economy and people's lives. Unfortunately, due to being covered in dust and unable to rest, there was no time to have further conversations.

The section of land twenty li west of "One Dragon" is currently under construction. Workers are assigned according to the area of land. According to what they said, "The most difficult road to build in this section is none other than the Parrot's Beak and Laoya Pass. The road is winding and narrow, and the rocky peaks are rugged and towering. To fill in the collapses, stone layers must be built from the bottom of the river, accumulating level by level to a height of more than ten zhang. To widen the narrow parts, rocks must be drilled and chiseled, which takes twice the effort and costs a lot."

Laoya City, thirty li away, has thick willows providing shade along the way, densely covering the sky. Travelers may suspect that they are in Lushan escaping the summer heat, and forget the hardships of the long journey in the summer season. The city has eighty or ninety households. Suddenly, there was a heavy rain, and the farmers were overjoyed at the long-awaited rain. The clouds dispersed, the rain stopped, and the air was fresh. Afterwards, passing through Baiya Village, Pujiadun, and Changli Town, there were especially abundant fruits such as walnuts, hawthorns, pears, and jujubes. Unfortunately, due to inconvenient transportation, they could not be transported far away to earn high prices. Moreover, there is always a clear spring under the trees, and the clear spring flows down to become fertile fields. Traveling through it, both shaded and drinking, one cannot bear to bid farewell. If one could cultivate and graze there, the feelings of homesickness would be indescribable.

Staying overnight at Gaomiao Town, the total journey was eighty li. The town has about 300 households and is the largest town under the jurisdiction of Ledu County. Shops selling oil, groceries, cloth, grain, and other goods are all readily available, which is the most lively market seen since Lanzhou. The town has one elementary school each for boys and girls. There are more than eighty boys and more than twenty girls. Most of them are over ten years old before starting school. Therefore, the age of students in the fifth and sixth grades is as old as high school students elsewhere. The sound of chanting could be heard far and wide early the next morning. Getting up early to study is commendable. On the west side of the town, a pox god temple is built on the fort, which the villagers greatly admire. The ignorant men and women do not know how to vaccinate their children in advance. Once smallpox is transmitted, they are terrified and reverently offer brocade curtains, fancy screens, and fancy shoes to the deity. The statue is obscured by the red and green decorations, and the depth of superstition can be said to be extreme.

On the 25th, departing from Gaomiao Town, women set up stalls along the willow shade to sell cooked eggs, potatoes, cold noodles, and other items. Shepherds and old men mostly wore green willow hats, which were very distinctive. Looking left at the mountain peaks, they were all silvery, and I knew that it had snowed heavily last night due to the cold weather. The climate in Qinghai is originally cold. Taking fruits as an example, the apricots and plums in Lanzhou have already matured and are on the market, while those produced here are only as big as fingers. It is expected that they will mature a month later. The maturation period of other melons and fruits is also later than elsewhere. Ledu County, fifteen li away, has a city built of earth, divided into inner and outer layers. A white pagoda is built on the southeastern corner of the city, with the slogan "Never Forget National Humiliation" written in red. The road follows the western part of the city. Below the city by the river is Donghu Park, which only has hundreds of tree seedlings and a bay of flowing water. The rest of the scenery seems to be still under cultivation. Outside the south gate, there are three springs gushing from the ground, developed into three ponds. Stones are piled around the ponds to raise the ground into a terrace. Railings are placed on the left and right of the terrace. A pavilion covers the pond, with the name "Yinhe Pavilion" and the pond called "Yinhe Pond," taking the meaning of harmony, joy, and health. I originally wanted to visit the city, but suddenly saw soldiers checking very carefully. To avoid trouble, I did not go.

Daxia, fifteen li away, has two mountains close together, with the Huangshui River flowing through them like a silver belt. The area produces placer gold, which the locals pan for using traditional methods. A group of five people earns two or three fen per day, which is truly a "neither starving to death nor getting rich" livelihood. The gorge is more than two li long, suddenly opening up, and one can see the beautiful scenery of fertile fields and lush forests again. Xiakou Fort, fifteen li away, has about a hundred households, plastered with notices with slogans such as "Publicly Prohibit Gambling, Violation Will Be Punished." Going further to Zhangjia Town, I stayed overnight. The town is fifty li east of Ledu and one hundred and twenty li north of the county seat (Huzhu) and seventy li west of Xining. Talking with a farmer named Wang, he claimed that "he sows five dou of land and can harvest five shi. After deducting five dou for seeds and paying one shi of grain, he only has three shi and five dou left. A family of five can barely make a living. However, in recent years, due to the frequent addition of taxes and the conversion of grain rations, not only does he feel that he cannot make ends meet, but he is also gradually in danger of freezing and starving. According to custom, renting one dou of land requires paying three dou of wheat in rent per year. The grain money and seeds are all borne by the tenant. Now, even if someone is hired to rent the land, exempting the rent of wheat and only hoping to bear the grain money, no one dares to accept." The area is rich in wood, especially poplar trees, which are planted in forests in the corners of fields to be used for building houses. Building a courtyard house, without covering the roof with tiles or plastering with lime, with three sides and nine rooms, costs only more than ten yuan in wages to live in a new house, which is a common occurrence. As for the big mountain south of the village, it looks lush and green, which is a natural forest of pine and cypress. I heard that the trees there are several spans in circumference and several zhang high, with a production area of about three hundred li around. Timber merchants cut and tie them into rafts, releasing them downstream, selling well in other provinces, which accounts for a major source of Qinghai's economy. The town has a Niangniang Temple (Temple of the Goddess), with two goddesses enshrined in the center. If rain and hail damage the crops, the villagers gather by beating gongs and carry the goddess in a sedan chair to tour the four mountains, even leaving her out in the rain for a long time in order to pray for clear weather. If there is a prolonged drought, the goddess is moved under the scorching sun or placed for a long time next to a spring to pray for heavy rain. Therefore, the goddess is carried out and welcomed in dozens of times a year. The villagers deceive themselves and cause trouble, which is too much.

The English and Japanese armies, on land and at sea, are

Yuguan Qindao Exercises

British Troops Conduct Field Exercises, Japanese Troops Conduct Street Warfare

Warships of Both Sides Gather in the Waters off Qindao

Tianjin Correspondence: British troops stationed in North China recently held their annual summer exercises. This matter, due to a statement issued by the head of the Japanese business affairs office in Yuguan, Mr. Iwai, caused serious negotiations between Britain and Japan. The British ambassador, Sir Miles Lampson, dismissed the Japanese statement while vacationing in Beidaihe, and the British troops, in accordance with the Boxer Protocol, set out from Qinhuangdao at 2:00 PM on July 31st with the 15th Company, consisting of 200 men, carrying eight cannons, twenty machine guns, and thirty-two horses. They proceeded to Erlangmiao near Yuguan, following the planned exercise schedule. The first day involved field maneuvers, the second day artillery practice, the third day a fortified point battle, the fourth day night combat, and the fifth day a battle for strategic points and an engagement battle, for a total of five days of exercises. The exercise area was centered on Erlangmiao, with Jiukou Pass as the base camp. The original plan was to march to Jiaoshan, but the Japanese troops stationed in Yuguan, considering the location a strategic point, sent a small detachment to garrison it, seemingly intending to occupy it first and prevent the British troops from ascending. Therefore, the British troops ceased their march to that area. While the British troops were exercising at Erlangmiao, the Japanese troops stationed in Yuguan, intending to demonstrate their power, also held street warfare exercises within the city with a part of the Kwantung Army. Approximately 500 troops participated, and on South Gate Outer Street, they displayed guns and cannons seized from our side during the battles of the Great Wall. From the afternoon of the 31st, when the exercises began, until the morning of the 4th, they fired cannons daily, echoing the sound of British guns and cannons at Erlangmiao. Before the British troops went to Erlangmiao, five British warships successively sailed from Weihaiwei harbor to Qinhuangdao. The flagship, HMS Folkestone, arrived at the port on the afternoon of the 31st. The ship had twenty-four cannons and carried 770 naval officers and sailors. The Naval Admiral also arrived in Qinhuangdao that evening on the Kailuan Mining Bureau's coal transport ship Fuping and went directly to Erlangmiao to review the exercises. On the 1st and 2nd of this month, British sailors twice landed in Qinhuangdao for parades to demonstrate their strength. Japanese soldiers stationed in Qinhuangdao also refused to be outdone, and from the 1st, they coordinated with Japanese sailors on Japanese warships anchored in the Qinhuangdao sea area to practice harbor seizure battles. At the same time, six Japanese warships belonging to the 1st and 2nd Fleets successively arrived at the harbor, taking a monitoring attitude towards the British warships. The atmosphere there was as tense as in the Yuguan area. Two hundred Japanese soldiers stationed in Tianjin also took the Beining train to Qinhuangdao on the afternoon of the 2nd to participate in the exercises, causing rumors to intensify. By 1:00 PM on the afternoon of the 4th, the British troops had completed their exercises at Erlangmiao and returned to Qinhuangdao, and the Japanese troops in Yuguan and Qindao ceased their exercises. However, the British and Japanese warships anchored in the Qindao sea area had not yet left. Today, more than 200 British soldiers stationed in Ping were heading east to Qindao. It is said that the British troop exercises are being conducted in sections. After the Qindao garrison exercises are completed, the garrisons in other areas will continue to conduct them. Therefore, the sound of British guns and cannons may still be heard in Yuguan in the coming days. Because the British troop exercises have not yet been completed, the Japanese army has also ordered troops along the Beining line to prepare for large-scale marches and exercises in Tangshan, Changli, Luanxian, Yuguan, Tanggu, Haizhen, and Qinhuangdao simultaneously. The date is not yet set, but it will roughly depend on the date of the second British exercise. It has been rumored that British soldiers were exercising in Yuguan and Japanese soldiers were exercising in Jiaoshan, and a stray bullet wounded a British soldier. After investigation with all parties concerned, this was not the case. However, on the morning of the 3rd, British sailors on British warships anchored in Qinhuangdao landed and encountered Japanese sailors. They argued over the right of way, and eventually, officers from both sides arrived to restrain their subordinates. The talk of a stray bullet may have been a misinterpretation of this incident. (5th)

Hubei Province Actively Rescues Disaster Victims

Disaster Relief and Famine Preparedness Committee Established, Work is Intense

Zhang Qun Determines Engineering Plans to Permanently Prevent Drought and Flooding

Hankou Correspondence: The Hubei Provincial Government, due to simultaneous drought and flooding causing widespread disasters throughout the province and millions of refugees starving, has specially organized a Disaster Relief and Famine Preparedness Committee as a dedicated organization to coordinate relief efforts, so that manpower and financial resources can be concentrated to achieve twice the results with half the effort. The committee was officially established on the 6th and elected He Hengfu, Meng Guangpeng, Li Fanyi, Ma Boyuan, and Zhou Weitang as standing committee members. The provincial government designated He Hengfu as the chairman, Meng Guangpeng as the director of the General Affairs Group, with Wang Kaihua as the deputy; Zhou Xingtang as the director of the Finance Group, with Jia Shiyi as the deputy; He Hengfu as the director of the Relief Group, with Chen Jingyu as the deputy; Li Fanyi as the director of the Public Works Group, with Yang Silian as the deputy; Wang Yiling as the director of the Audit Group, with Su Taiyu as the deputy; and Ma Boyuan as the director of the Investigation Group, with Chen Huaizhong as the deputy. On the 7th, the first meeting was held and the following key issues were decided: (1) The standard for the distribution of relief funds is 60% for work relief, 20% for agricultural relief, and 20% for emergency relief, with the responsible group drafting a plan. (2) An investigation into the disaster situation in various areas will be carried out by the Investigation Group, which will convene the China International Famine Relief Commission, the Civil Affairs Department, the Cooperative Guidance Committee, the Rural Financial Relief Office, and other relevant organizations to allocate investigation work and formulate a plan to be submitted to the committee. Furthermore, as standing committee members He Hengfu and Zhou Xingtang are currently in Lushan, telegrams were sent requesting their return to Hubei to preside over the committee's affairs. Provincial government chairman Zhang Qun stated, "Since the beginning of summer this year, the weather has been arid, and there has been no rain for a long time. The eastern and southern parts of Hubei, as well as the counties near the provincial capital, have been severely affected. Rice, beans, hemp, and cotton have all withered, and the autumn harvest is already hopeless. The severity of the disaster is so great, the suffering of the people can be imagined. On the other hand, in the upper reaches of the Xiang River, mountain torrents have erupted, and the Xiang River and the East Jing River have suddenly surged, with water levels three feet higher than in the past twenty years. Embankments in the coastal counties have collapsed, causing further flooding. Currently, the flood disaster is not yet extremely serious, but the drought-stricken areas are expanding daily, which is truly heartbreaking. The provincial government's solutions to treat the symptoms and address the root causes have long been drafted. What we hope for from the central government is not only temporary relief to treat the symptoms, but especially fundamental famine preparedness measures. The so-called root cause solution is to study how to prevent floods and how to use water to prevent drought. This is a major issue that cannot be solved with a small amount of money, nor can it be accomplished in a short period of time. A preliminary engineering plan has been determined, with a total cost of 2.4 million yuan. The plan can be divided into four parts: (1) Installing water pumps; (2) Installing siphons and culverts; (3) Digging ponds and embankments; (4) Dredging ditches. Our province straddles the Yangtze and Han rivers, with 36 counties relying on embankments for protection. In the past, the government and the people only focused on embankments and did not pay attention to the problems of drainage and irrigation within the embankments. Even if the embankments are intact, they suffer from waterlogging in the spring and summer, and drought causes a lack of water for irrigation. It is now planned to select important embankments and install 50 pumping stations to pump water from the Yangtze and Han rivers for irrigation during droughts and drain accumulated water to benefit farmland. This project requires 15,000 yuan per station, totaling 750,000 yuan. If the embankment area is small and the terrain and water level do not require the installation of a pumping station, siphons can be installed on the top of the embankment or culverts can be buried at the bottom of the embankment, which is cheaper and less labor-intensive than pumping stations. It is planned to select 30 locations, costing 10,000 yuan each, for a total of 300,000 yuan. As for fields in high-lying and mountainous areas, they traditionally rely on ponds and embankments for water storage, but their scale is small and they are gradually silting up. It is planned to dig 500 new ponds in areas of northern and eastern Hubei that are in greater need, each with an area of 3 mu and a standard depth of 7 meters, costing a total of 650,000 yuan. Furthermore, ditch drainage is particularly important. It is planned to excavate distribution and branch ditches, totaling approximately 500 kilometers in length, with an average area of 22,067 square meters, costing a total of 1.1 million yuan. The total cost of the above four projects is 2.4 million yuan, with earthwork accounting for two-thirds, or 1.8 million yuan, which can all be used for work relief to aid disaster victims." (7th)

Wuhu Rice Temporarily Banned from Export

Suppressing Rice Prices, No More Than Ten Yuan Per Stone

Wuhu Correspondence: This area is suffering from a severe drought, and rice prices are soaring. High-quality machine-milled rice is selling for as much as 11.67 yuan per stone, and lower grades are also around 11 yuan. At retail stores, one yuan can only buy nine sheng of rice. A month ago, rice prices were still around six yuan, but now they have risen more than twofold, a phenomenon only seen after the great flood of twenty years ago. Wuhu Port is a gathering area for rice and grain in southern Anhui. Guangdong, Yantai, Ningbo, and various garrisoned troops all have permanent purchasing agencies, and exports are no less than 8 million stones per year. Now that selling prices are skyrocketing, not only are outside buyers absorbing as much as possible, but also counties in the interior of this province are coming to Wuhu to purchase and stock up in preparation for rice shortages. Market prices are still expected to continue rising, and the livelihoods of ordinary people are increasingly panicked as a result. Therefore, Wang Baozhai, the Administrative Inspector of the Second District, specially convened a meeting at the County Chamber of Commerce at 9:00 this morning, gathering leaders from the rice and grain transport industry, the rice industry, the miscellaneous grain and rice industry, the rice husking industry, and the rice milling industry to discuss relief measures. Chairman Wang presided over the meeting, and it was generally agreed that the soaring rice prices were causing unspeakable hardship for ordinary people and also affecting the social mood. It was decided to suppress rice prices, with the highest price for machine-milled rice not to exceed 10 yuan per stone. In order to prevent local rice shortages and maintain the people's food supply, exports of rice and grain will be suspended from today (the 7th) until the 30th of this month. The future situation will be monitored, but the circulation of new grain will still be allowed in order to avoid affecting the counties. The above two resolutions were officially announced and implemented by the Commissioner. If this can suppress rice prices, people's hearts will be greatly stabilized. (6th)

Flooding in Northern Shandong Rivers

Yucheng's Zhao Niu River and Deng Jin River Breach One After Another

Vast Disaster Area within Qihe County, Fields and Houses Washed Away

Jinan Correspondence: After the dredging of the Zhao Niu River in northern Shandong, only the middle reaches within Qihe County were not dredged. After the heavy rains ten days ago, the river water rose sharply, and the water in the Zhao Niu River could not drain into the Tuhai River, leading to flooding and breaches. In addition, the Zhao Niu River backflowed, and the Deng Jin River also breached. Initially, on July 26th, the Deng Jin River breached on the west bank of Zhujia Daokou. On the 29th, the Zhao Niu River also breached at Jiehekou. The two rivers converged southward, inundating approximately 100 hectares of farmland. The water level of the Deng Jin River did not decrease slightly. On the 4th of this month, it breached again on the east bank of Zhujia Daokou, with the water heading northeast directly through Qihe County into the Tuhai River. The water surface was two to three li wide, up to eight or nine li, and more than twenty li long. Fields and houses were washed away, and the autumn crops that were about to ripen were completely submerged. The disaster is extremely severe. Within Yucheng County, fortunately, the rescue and plugging were timely, and the disaster was avoided. The Construction Department previously sent technician Meng Xianzheng to investigate the relationship between the Deng Jin River, Zhao Niu River, Tizhang River, and Luo River in order to plan for the aftermath. He is currently inspecting. The following is a record of Meng's telegram reporting the river breaches: "I inspected the breaches of the Zhao Niu River and Deng Jin River in Yucheng and the dangerous works along the coast on August 1st. The Zhao Niu River breached at Jiehekou on July 29th, about 50 meters wide. The Deng Jin River breached at Zhujia Daokou on July 26th at noon. These two breaches converge in District 2, inundating approximately 200 hectares of land. Local residents built a water barrier at Shuangmiaozi to prevent the water from spreading southward. At 3:00 AM on August 4th, the Deng Jin River breached again on the east bank of Zhujia Daokou, with the water heading northeast directly towards Gan Yutou, rushing into the Tuhai River. The affected area is approximately 20 li long and two to three li to eight or nine li wide. Ninety percent of the area is under the jurisdiction of Qihe. Currently, there are seven dangerous works on the north bank of the Zhao Niu River: Qiliquiao, Zhangshui Daokou, Baimiaotang, Shangyoujun, Zhangzhuang, Jiehekou, and the west bank of Boluotun and Qiaozhaowangzhuang. Fortunately, the county magistrate and the four sections have been urging the people to work hard to protect the area, and most of Yucheng has been spared from the disaster. I am currently planning to inspect the relationship between the Danzhang River, Luo River, Tuhai River, and Zhao Niu River in order to plan for the aftermath. I hereby submit this report and request that it be forwarded to the director of the department for review. Your humble servant, Meng Xianzheng." (5th)

Weihaiwei

The Process of Preparing for the Establishment of an Airport

Weihai Correspondence: Xu Dongfan, the commissioner of Weihaiwei Management, believes that the inconvenience of land transportation in the port poses a great obstacle to local prosperity and industrial development. He urgently hopes to leverage the power of aviation to provide relief. Because Weihai occupies an important international position, all facilities have been observed by both Chinese and foreigners since our country recovered it. Moreover, Weihai Port is the base of our country's Third Fleet in peacetime. During the summer and autumn seasons each year, the British fleet moors here, with up to 8,000 British officers and soldiers. The comings and goings of warships from other countries are even more difficult to estimate. During the summer, there are at least a thousand foreign tourists and expatriates, and there are also many Chinese people who come here for travel or to escape the summer heat. The round trips of these passengers and mail rely entirely on maritime transportation. Land transportation lacks adequate connections. Passengers who wish to travel quickly and mail that needs to arrive quickly really feel the need to use aviation. This is also an urgent need in reality.

The Changfeng area of Weihai originally had an airport with complete equipment. It is said that the Management Office recently expanded the field to the size of the Qingdao Airport, which is sufficient for aircraft to take off and land. If the China National Aviation Corporation's aircraft traveling on the Shanghai-Ping Line can detour through Weihai, it can use this field. Commissioner Xu also worried that the company might have difficulties with the increased expenses of establishing a station. Therefore, he resolutely agreed to handle the airport affairs on behalf of the Management Office to reduce the company's burden in order to realize this as soon as possible. Local people also expressed their sympathy for this initiative. Therefore, starting in late May of this year, negotiations with the China National Aviation Corporation began, with several letters and telegrams exchanged. Subsequently, Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Transportation was asked to preside over and urge the matter to benefit the local area. Several letters and telegrams were received from Minister Zhu, all of which promised to instruct the company to plan and proceed accordingly. At the same time, Commissioner Xu used his personal relationships to send letters to Lou Guanglai, the director of the Postal Department of the Ministry of Communications, to help mediate, and he also agreed to assist. However, in reality, the company also had considerable difficulties, which could not be achieved overnight. Because the aircraft currently flying between Shanghai and Ping have a speed of 110 kilometers per hour, if the flight time is extended, the pilots will inevitably be too tired. In addition, detouring through Weihai requires crossing the sea, which cannot be accommodated by aircraft designed to travel on land. Because of this obstacle, on June 26th, the Ministry of Communications forwarded a telegram from the company stating that "when faster aircraft are replaced in the future, a branch line may be opened in Weihai to connect with the main line." The company's letter to Commissioner Xu on June 15th also contained the same statement. Minister Zhu's reply on July 11th also stated that "it would be most appropriate for the company to plan and open a branch line in the future." It can be seen that the company's current inability to quickly open the Weihai airport is due to the perceived difficulties in existing aircraft technology.

According to recent reliable information from the Ministry of Transportation, the airline will purchase new aircraft from the United States in November of this year, with the speed increasing to 180 kilometers per hour, saving one-third of the time compared to the current aircraft. These aircraft can certainly open a branch line in Weihai to connect with the main line. At that time, there will be no difficulty in adding an airport. Therefore, it is still possible for passengers and mail to and from Weihai to use aviation in the near future.

Songjiang Prefecture Orders the Abolition of Miscellaneous Taxes in this County

The National Finance Conference resolved to select miscellaneous taxes that are close to harsh and meticulous in various provinces, cities, and counties and abolish them separately, and find other means of compensation to alleviate the people's difficulties. The Jiangsu Provincial Government first complied and successively reviewed the harsh and meticulous miscellaneous taxes in various counties, whether or not they were included in the budget, and ordered their abolition in stages in order to comply with the central government's intention to care for the people's hardships. Changzhou Murderer of Ten Years Ago Arrested

Guo Jinyuan, Gao Lianbao and other bandits from Wu Yi killed Xiangmin Xu Baisheng in the 12th year of the Republic of China. Afterwards, Yan Pengcheng, a Hubei native, who lived in Wolong Township in the county and had relatives with Xu Baisheng, presented a petition to the official office to arrest the murderer, which resulted in another grievance with the bandits. On January 17th, the 14th year of the Republic of China, Yan Pengcheng and his wife were kidnapped by bandits Guo Jinyuan, Zhang Sanda, etc. while watching the lights in the nearby Land Temple. When they arrived at Xiaolonggangkou, they threw Yan Pengcheng and his wife into the river and drowned them. Then, Guo fled to another place and has not been arrested until now. Yan Changyun, Yan's son, has now grown up and is determined to avenge this irreconcilable hatred. He went out to investigate. Unexpectedly, the bandits were brought to justice. Guo and Zhang were sent to the county court for another bandit case. After Yan Changyun confirmed that it was true, he filed a lawsuit with the county court yesterday (7th) according to law, requesting that they be brought to justice in order to comfort his parents in the afterlife.

Nantong Jiangbei Drought Disaster Severe

Since the rainfall in the Jiangbei Tong area and the Huainan reclamation area in the middle of last month, the weather has been extremely hot and clear, and the drought is now becoming severe again. Officials and people in Nantong are working together to set up a water station in Yaogang, open electric pumps, and draw river water to rescue the disaster.

Haimen The Ministry of Justice Sends Personnel to Investigate the Case Against the Trial Officer

Deng Gongsan, a trial officer in this county, has often acted improperly in handling lawsuits, which has led to the parties concerned accusing Deng in the High Court and the Ministry of Justice. Although Judge Long of the Nantong Court came to Hai to investigate, the true facts have not been obtained. Now that the Ministry of Justice believes that the trial officer has been repeatedly accused, it has specially commissioned the Bao Mountain County Magistrate to investigate. Xu Yingtu, a section member specially sent by the Bao Mountain County Magistrate, came to Hai the day before yesterday and stayed at the An Hotel. When a reporter visited him, he reported as follows: This time, I was ordered to come to Hai to investigate the case against the trial officer in your county. There are four cases, three criminal cases and one civil case, most of which belong to bribery and dereliction of duty. There is a case of a corpse in Songji Port. I have already gone to the scene to investigate in detail and reviewed all the documents in the county government. The facts are clear. The remaining three cases are still under serious investigation. Once all the cases are fully investigated, I must return to Bao and report.

Nursing Home Abuses the Elderly

Yang Dabing, the director of the nursing home in this county, is engaged in business and has no time to advise on the affairs of the nursing home. Huang Gengxin and Lu Yousong are responsible for handling the affairs, but Huang and Lu often do not comply with the regulations and arbitrarily abuse the elderly. They only give porridge and wheat rice once a day, and withhold and do not pay the work wages. The day before yesterday, an old man surnamed Fan went to Huang et al. to recover the withheld wages, which angered him. He was tied to a pillar and severely whipped. Fan wailed for help, which was unbearable to hear. Then, all the elderly people pleaded for him, and he was released. Now, Chen Baigeng and 20 other people believe that Huang and Lu's actions are contrary to humanity. Yesterday (6th), they specially submitted a petition to the county government, requesting that they be strictly investigated.

Water Conservancy Dispute Between Zhenjiang Jindan Counties

Regarding the case of Danyang farmers building a dam on the Xiangcao River to block the tide, harming the downstream water conservancy of Jintan, after vigorous efforts by various groups in Jintan, the provincial government has ordered Danyang County to dismantle the lower dam and reasonably reduce the upper dam. However, after many days, the Danyang County Magistrate Yan has not complied, and the people downstream in Jintan are desperate due to the water shortage. Public sentiment is stirred, and they all want to go to open the dam themselves. Considering the serious situation, the Jintan representative stationed in the provincial capital is deeply concerned that the people will take risks. Therefore, he is still making every effort to request the provincial authorities to send a special commissioner to open the dam to avoid causing trouble.

The Su Family's Mouth in Funing Was Looted by Bandits

At about 2 PM yesterday, in the Su Family's Mouth area of the tenth district of this county, bandits led by Xia Sandiedie, the staff officer of bandit Zhang Zhigao, suddenly appeared with 60-70 bandits, each armed with guns and bullets. They entered the town from North Street and surrounded the local police station. Police officer He Naijian led the police to resist, but they were outnumbered. The bandits occupied the town, looted wantonly, set fires, and kidnapped more than 80 men and women as hostages, heading northwest. Zhu Shoupeng, the leader of the guard detachment stationed in Fenggu Village, and the Yilin tax police and the Public Security Bureau heard the news and led teams to suppress them. They rescued more than 60 hostages halfway. The bandits fled to the Tongying area.

Robbery Occurred in Jiaxing Dongzha Town

The home of Shen A'san in Tianjiwan, Dongzha Town, Jiaxing, was suddenly visited by eight robbers the night before last. Armed with weapons, five guarded the front door, and three entered the house to search and loot. They ransacked trunks and chests, stealing 40 silver dollars, 13 paper dollars, six carts of silk, and several pieces of gold jewelry. When a patrol police officer passed by, the robbers immediately fled. Although they were pursued, nothing was gained.
