Local News

Hurricane Passed Shanghai Eastward Yesterday Afternoon

Only the left wing with a force of six winds swept over the city.

High tides caused water accumulation in low-lying roads.

Ordinary buildings suffered minor damage, and navigation resumed.

The hurricane that approached Shanghai in recent days passed over Shanghai yesterday morning and continued to move northwest-west, remaining at sea. At 10 AM yesterday, the hurricane reached the east side of Daji Mountain, about 80 miles from Shanghai. According to the report from the Daji Mountain Observatory received by the Xujiahui Observatory, from 6 AM to 9 AM on the 8th, the north wind reached a force of ten, which is rarely encountered inland. It is strong enough to uproot trees and cause other damage. The speed of ten winds can reach 53 to 63 miles per hour. When the hurricane approached Shanghai yesterday morning, the Huangpu River was surging wildly, and no ships were sailing on the river. Fortunately, it did not reach the city, so the wind gradually subsided in the afternoon, and the heat wave was greatly reduced. The highest temperature yesterday was only 81.5 degrees, which is almost 20 degrees lower than Sunday (99.7).

Swept Over Shanghai

This time, the two hurricanes merged in the Pacific Ocean, so their strength was very great, reaching as many as ten winds. At 10 AM yesterday, the observatory reported that the main force of the hurricane had reached Daji Mountain at 31 degrees north latitude and 123 degrees east longitude, outside the eastern port of Shanghai, with a force of ten. The wind speed was 27 meters per second, or 97 kilometers per hour, and the direction was north-northwest or north. At 11 AM, the direction was north-northwest, so only the left wing of the hurricane swept over Shanghai, with a total of six winds. The observatory reported again at 2 PM yesterday that the left wing of the hurricane had passed Shanghai, and its main force was at 32 degrees north latitude and 124 degrees east longitude, heading north-northeast, crossing the Yellow Sea, and blowing towards Korea.

High Tide

After the hurricane swept over Shanghai yesterday afternoon, it was blowing in the ocean, fortunately not landing, so the city and inland areas did not suffer wind damage, but the coastal areas must have suffered some damage. The Huangpu River in Shanghai rose due to the seawater being blown in by the wind, causing the river to rise. At about 5 AM yesterday, the Bund and North Sichuan Road were flooded with water reaching several inches, but it quickly receded.

Customs Warning

The Jianghai Customs received a report from the observatory the night before last that the hurricane had blown to the Wenzhou sea area. To avoid misfortunes for ships on the Jianghai River, a black mark was specially hung on the roof, and two red lights were lit at the same time to warn ships to stop entering and leaving the Wusongkou. It was changed to a black cross warning ball yesterday morning, indicating that the hurricane was approaching the city. The black ball was removed at 11:15 AM.

Damage Overview

Although the main force of the hurricane did not reach the city yesterday, its left wing still had a strong wind force of six, causing damage to many ordinary buildings in the East Shanghai area. In particular, telephone lines in Wusong, Zhenru, Jiangwan, Zhabei, and road construction areas outside the concession were mostly blown off and could not be connected. The telephone company sent personnel to repair them in separate locations, and all were repaired by the afternoon. There were also some telephone poles and trees that were uprooted, and many store signs on various roads were destroyed.

Overturned Boat in Huangpu River

At about 11 AM yesterday, Chen Shifa (33 years old) from Hubei was newly piloting a kiln cargo ship from north to south, passing the Huangpu River surface at the Jiuda Pier in Nanshi. At that time, a hurricane hit Shanghai, with heavy rain and huge waves. The ship was weak and could not withstand it, and it overturned. A large number of kiln goods and the shipowner and crew on board also fell into the river, shouting for help. The water patrol team of the local Municipal Public Security Bureau heard the news and immediately sent captains Zhu and Li, leading a large number of police officers, on patrol boats to the scene. They rescued many crew members, including Shao Changmu, and recovered many kiln goods that had sunk to the bottom of the river. However, the shipowner Chen Shifa and his partner Song Xianghe disappeared after falling into the river. At the time, the police thought they had been swept away by the huge waves and had no chance of survival. Unexpectedly, at about 1 PM, several ruffians saw that the bottom of the ship was facing the sky, floating on the river surface, and no one was guarding it. They immediately went forward and used iron tools to dig a large hole in the bottom of the ship, planning to steal items. Suddenly, they saw two men in the cabin of the ship. When the ship overturned, they were in the cabin and could not escape, and they could not pry open the bottom of the ship, so they were suffocated in the cabin, with their eyes closed, waiting for death to come. The ruffians tried to rescue them from the water, and they were able to be reborn. Upon questioning, they were identified as the shipowner Chen Shifa and his partner Song Xianghe. However, when the ship overturned, it sank to the bottom of the river and then floated up, drifting on the river surface for a total of two hours. Chen and the others were suffocated in the cabin, immersed in water, but did not drown. It can be said to be a miracle.

Collapsed Walls and Sheds

(1) The house of the Zhao family at No. 1, Jiwu Lane, Fangbang Road, in the city, collapsed due to disrepair and old age. At about 1 PM yesterday, a brick wall behind the Zhao family's house suddenly collapsed due to wind and rain, crushing many sundries such as tables and stools. Fortunately, no one was injured. (2) Yan Xinglong, 33 years old, from Changzhou, has been running a stove at No. 249, Fangbang Road, in the city. At about 10 AM yesterday, when the wind was strong and the rain was heavy, the east wall of the stove suddenly collapsed. At that time, Qiu Delin from Nanjing was sipping tea there and could not escape. He was crushed under the rubble and seriously injured. Yan Xinglong saw it and quickly called his colleagues to rescue Qiu and sent him to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. (3) Yao Lansheng, 30 years old, a local resident, lives at No. 62, Gaodun Road, in the city. Recently, due to the hot weather, he built a reed shed in his courtyard to block the sunlight. Unexpectedly, at about 9 AM yesterday, when the hurricane came, the shed was weak and could not withstand it and collapsed, pressing on the chimney on the roof of the neighboring Liu family at No. 60. However, the chimney was made of brick and mud and was already old, so it collapsed and fell into the courtyard of Sun Lizhi (35 years old) from Yangzhou at No. 58 next door. At that time, Sun happened to be standing there, so the broken bricks fell on Yao's head, causing him to bleed profusely and collapse to the ground unconscious. Sun's family heard the sound and rushed over and quickly sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Ningbo Ships Suspended

The Ningbo passenger ship Ningxing of the Sanbei Company had already boarded passengers the day before yesterday. When they received the observatory's announcement that the hurricane was blowing from Ningbo to Shanghai, the company immediately announced that the Ningxing would suspend its voyage and stop exporting. At that time, the passengers were quite dissatisfied and negotiated with the crew. After the shipowner declared the danger of sailing, the tickets were returned. The Taikoo New Beijing and Ningshao Ningshao ships from Ningbo to Shanghai did not sail because the hurricane had arrived in Ningbo by 10 AM on the 7th. Taikoo Ningshao Ningbo flights have no ships to Ningbo today.

Returned Midway

The China Merchants Bureau's New Jiangtian ship departed from Shanghai at 4:30 PM on the 7th. When it reached outside Sanjia Water, the ship received a warning from the observatory that the hurricane was about to hit head-on. The shipowner of the New Jiangtian received the news and ordered the ship to turn back. It was already late at night, but the hurricane was encountered on the way back. Fortunately, the express ship returned to Shanghai quickly, but the passengers on board were deeply unhappy. The ship is now scheduled to depart for Ningbo again at 4 PM today.

Fujian Ships Blocked

The sea ships sailing from Shanghai to Fuzhou on the 7th included Qingpu, Songpu, Shengan, Wanxiang, Guangli, and Gongping. When they sailed outside Wusongkou, each sea ship received a strong wind warning from the observatory and chose a safe sea area outside Wusongkou to anchor and avoid the wind. Yesterday, each ship sent a telegram to Shanghai reporting that it had not yet departed and would depart after the wind subsided. There were also many sea ships to Fujian that postponed their departure date due to the hurricane.

Sea Ships Sheltering from the Wind

The sea ships sailing from Shanghai to the North and South Oceans the day before yesterday, and the ships sailing from Shantou, Xiamen, Guangzhou, Yantai, and Tianjin to Shanghai, which were supposed to enter the port yesterday, were blocked by the hurricane and did not dare to venture. In total, there were more than 20 sea ships entering and leaving the port, anchoring and sheltering from the wind outside Wusongkou, from Sanjia Water, Tongsha, to the Sheshan Ocean area. Therefore, only three sea ships, Yichang and others, entered Wusong yesterday afternoon, and four ships, Shihe, Anqing, Xingshi, and Ruihe, came from the Yangtze River. The customs patrol ship Haijing also returned to Shanghai after patrolling at sea. As for the departing ships, in addition to the four ships Longhe, Shashi, Jiangjing, and Jiahe from the Yangtze River, the sea ship Taikoo's Jinan has been changed to depart tomorrow morning. The others are Dala's Grand President and a Japanese ship going to the ocean.

Inspecting Seawalls

At about 1 AM yesterday, Wusongkou was invaded by a hurricane. The tide rose sharply, and the rain was heavy at dawn, with waves surging. The sailing ships in the Songkou Huangpu River all took refuge in the inner harbor. The Baotaiwan lighthouse and weather vane all had special warnings to ensure safe navigation. The Baoshan seawall has been repaired by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and the project is 70-80% complete. It is said that it can be fully completed before the tide of this session (August 3rd of the lunar calendar). It is currently being rushed to complete. However, the seawalls in the Wusong area have many breaches since the Japanese artillery fire on January 28th. Local groups have been worried about this and have repeatedly appealed for repairs, but the Municipal Bureau of Public Works believes that it is not yet necessary, so it has not been implemented. It is now heard that the Municipal Bureau of Public Works has officially tendered for the East and West seawall projects, and it will likely begin construction soon. Yesterday afternoon, Wusong party and government leaders Wang Cheng'e, Tang Zuanzhi, Wu Renqi, Yao Guangnai, Yin Gongtian, and others personally went to inspect the current status of the seawalls along the Outer Bund and Baotaiwan area.

River Preparedness

Although the Jianghai Customs hurricane warning black cross was removed at noon, the remaining wind in Shanghai was still strong. Barges, civilian ships, small ships, sampans, boats, etc. on the Huangpu River are still on alert. Those who sailed into Suzhou Creek and Laogang to shelter from the wind have not yet departed by yesterday afternoon. There was very little cargo barging to and fro on the river.

Cotton Damaged

Cotton is currently being harvested, and a hurricane is sweeping the coasts of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, with very strong winds, causing many flowers and fruits to be blown off. Weak branches are also easily broken, causing unsustainable losses for farmers. Yesterday, the cotton market price on the Yarn and Cloth Exchange rose by 40-50 cents, both near and far.

Power Pole Blown Down

West of Huta Road, a wooden power line pole suddenly fell down at about 7 AM yesterday due to the hurricane. A boy named Chen Xiaosanzi from Jiangbei, about six or seven years old, happened to be passing by and was suddenly struck in the head, causing his skull to shatter and bleed profusely. He immediately fell to the ground and died. Passersby saw it and quickly reported it to the police officer at the post, who transferred it to the local Tu Dibao to report to the local court for verification.

Yu Youren Went to Beijing Yesterday

Yu Youren, President of the Control Yuan, came to Shanghai for medical treatment due to illness and has been here for many days. Now that Yu's condition has improved and he has regained his health, and the affairs of the Yuan need to be handled personally, he took the night express train to Beijing last night. Accompanying Yu were Chu Minyi and Chen Ce.

City Chamber of Commerce Telegram to the Southwest Political Committee

Abolish Special Taxes on Domestic Goods

The boycott of yarn factories in China should be clearly defined.

It is inappropriate to make domestic goods manufacturers perish together.

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Southwest Political Affairs Committee and the Guangdong Provincial Government yesterday (briefly): "On the 7th of this month, we received a letter from the China Chemical Industry Society, stating that it was heard that Guangdong industry and commerce, citing that Shanghai factories mostly have foreign investment and dumped goods in Guangdong, vigorously advocated and demanded that the provincial authorities implement taxes to protect the local industry. It was also heard that the local chambers of commerce had been convened by the authorities and agreed to set up a bureau to collect special taxes on imported goods and goods imported from outside the province. Please quickly telegraph the provincial authorities to inquire about the details and request the cancellation of the original proposal to collect special taxes on domestic goods in order to protect national products." The Chamber of Commerce investigated that Chinese merchants' machines imitating foreign goods had preferential treatment during the Qing Dynasty Lijing was not reduced, only when exported a positive tax of one in one hundred and five was completed, they can pass through the whole country and avoid re-levy. Now that Lijing has been cut, national products, whether they are natural products or manufactured products, except when they are transshipped, pay a transshipment tax at the first customs according to regulations, and no other taxes are collected between provinces. This is a good policy for merchants after the reduction of Lijing. The bad system left over from the former Qing Dynasty for more than 70 years has just been deleted, how can it be restored? If according to the suggestions of the Guangdong industry and commerce community, the special tax is in name, but in reality Lijing, it is contrary to the policy of promoting domestic goods. And in terms of the current special tax system in Guangdong Province, it is only limited to foreign goods, and if the scope is expanded, it will make domestic goods suffer the same destruction. At a time when commerce is depressed, only South China has a dense population and a relatively stable order, and there is still room for commodity promotion. If special tax barriers are also set up and strict prevention and control are carried out, then our country's commodities will be rejected abroad and again rejected at home. Surrounded on all sides and unable to move, how can industry not perish together? Assuming that the authorities of all provinces hear the news and rise up in response, competing in the name of protecting local products and imposing special taxes on goods from outside the province, wouldn't the goods from Guangdong Province sold to all provinces be affected in the same way? Careful consideration of both sides may not be beneficial to the industry and commerce of Guangdong Province. Tracing the origin of this idea, it is nothing more than that Shanghai factories inevitably have foreign establishments. Then the conclusion is still in maintaining national factories and resisting foreign factories. It is more appropriate to clearly distinguish the boundaries and not to lump them together. For example, there are also national factories that are set up in Hong Kong, how can they be regarded as foreign goods because they come from Hong Kong? Moreover, foreign merchants have the right to set up factories in China in all treaty ports, not only in Shanghai. The new industries run by Chinese people are mostly located in treaty ports for the convenience of using power. Once this end is opened, the industrial products of any port in the country will not be able to be sold in Guangdong Province due to heavy taxes, and the damage is more than just Shanghai. According to what the Chamber of Commerce has heard, foreign merchants have set up factories in Shanghai. Except for the textile industry, which is more common, and the cigarette industry, which is more influential, which one of the others is more Chinese factories and fewer foreign factories? The tax authorities in charge of taxes have records to check and can easily check. If Guangdong Province is using the maintenance of national factories as a policy, it seems that it should conduct a detailed investigation and strictly define the scope to avoid losing the overall situation and making national products fall into a position that is difficult to recover forever. Based on the foregoing, I dare to represent all the domestic goods manufacturers in Shanghai to make urgent appeals. I only hope that you will preside over the matter. If the special tax item is inevitable, it is necessary to handle it carefully, so that domestic goods manufacturers will not be implicated and perish together. It is fortunate. Shanghaishi Chamber of Commerce bowed and praised,

Ministry of Finance

Instructions to the Bankers Association

No violation of the Savings Law is allowed.

The Shanghai Bankers Association believes that according to the provisions of Article 9 of the Savings Bank Law promulgated and implemented by the National Government, each savings bank should deposit one-quarter of the total amount of savings deposits in government bonds and treasury bills calculated at the market price to the Central Bank for safekeeping, and obtain a receipt for submission to the Ministry for verification. This is practically difficult to implement. The Ministry of Finance was previously asked to postpone the implementation. It is now known that the Ministry of Finance, after receiving the report, specially instructed the Bankers Association yesterday that the request for a postponement of implementation is difficult to approve. The reporter from Xinxin News Agency now finds and records the original text of its instructions as follows: Ministry of Finance Instructions, Shanghai Money Letter No. 1, to the Shanghai Banking Industry Association, a report, for the savings bank law has not been decided before, for the Article 9 of the law, the depositing of public debt treasury bills section, intended to humbly ask for a postponement of implementation, report received, check the submission of government public debt treasury bills, in order to protect the interests of savings depositors, increase the credibility of the bank, not only the savings bank law clearly stipulates, namely each bank's self-established savings regulations, approved by the Ministry, also have the same regulations, Now the Savings Bank Law, the National Government has already promulgated and implemented, the Ministry should follow the regulations, and each bank's self-established regulations should not be violated. The request for a postponement of implementation should not be discussed. This custody method has also been requested by the Ministry in a letter to the Central Bank to properly stipulate. The types and numbers of assets that guarantee credibility should be verified by the Ministry at any time, and each bank should follow the instructions. There is absolutely no inconvenience. As for the various points in the proposed amendment to the Savings Bank Law that are difficult to implement, they are not related to Article 9 and have been submitted by the Ministry to the Executive Yuan for consultation. Together, please know. This order,

Ministry of Finance

Building a Great Ministry Treasury

Divided into two rooms, each with a capacity of 100 million yuan

Address: Central Mint, completed by the end of the year

Xinsheng News Agency said that the Ministry of Finance has decided to build a great ministry treasury at the Central Mint, divided into two rooms, each with a capacity of 100 million to 130 million yuan. It is scheduled to be completed on December 20th, and the bidding will be opened and construction will begin on schedule. The details are as follows: Construction of the Treasury.

The Ministry of Finance has decided to build a ministry treasury at the Central Mint on the north bank of the Suzhou River at the end of Gordon Road in Shanghai, 100 feet wide and 140 feet long, divided into two rooms, each with a capacity of 100 million to 130 million yuan. The net height of the treasury is 15 feet. It is designed by Zhuang Jun Architecture, and the bidding has been invited. The bidding will be opened at 10 AM on August 15th. Drawings and specifications can be obtained from Zhuang Jun Architect's Office.

Treasury Engineering

The treasury engineering is as follows: The treasury walls are 24 inches thick, the inner 10 inches are made of domestic machine-made fire bricks and cement mortar. The treasury wall ground, top, pillars, beams, stairs, foundations, roofs, etc. are all constructed of reinforced concrete. The inside of the treasury is paved with domestic mineral bricks and the walls are tiled with face bricks. The outside ground, stairs, etc. are all made of cement and copper sand, leveled in blocks, and cement retaining walls are made, 5 feet high. The outside aisle is divided into two layers, and the method of making the interlayer ground is the same as that of the outside ground. All are made of flat roofs, with water falling on all sides, using oil felt, oil paste, and small stones.

Completed by the End of the Year

The tender opening office has set the opening date for the 15th of this month. All successful bidders will sign a contract with the Ministry of Finance, stipulating that the contractor should complete the entire project by December 20th, 1923 of the Republic of China. Rain, etc. shall not be postponed, otherwise, a loss of 100 yuan per day of postponement will be compensated.

Japanese Embassy Spokesperson

Denies Arimaya's Passivity

There is also no intention to return home.

The Far East News Agency said that the Japanese Ambassador to China, Arimaya, had once been rumored to be dismissed. Later, this saying gradually subsided. However, in the past two days, the Japanese newspapers have once again carried that Arimaya suddenly had the intention to resign and planned to return to China in September. The successor will be Tani Masao, the current councillor of the Puppet Embassy. A reporter from the Far East News Agency went to the Japanese Embassy yesterday to find out what was going on. The spokesperson solemnly denied to the reporter that all the rumors were pure speculation and were not worth believing. Moreover, the ambassador has no intention of returning to China in September.

Extension of the Tax Reduction Period for County Deeds for Three Months

The Shanghai County Government has now received an order from the province that the land and house deed tax, a reduction of six parts and three of the micro-sale, has been on trial for three months since May and is now limited. A special extension of three months to the end of October is intended to reflect both solicitude and warning. After receiving the order, the county government, in addition to the announcement, yesterday also ordered the district township public office to notify each household that all untaxed white deeds under the name of the public should come to the county to pay the tax in full during the tax reduction period. If the deadline is not paid, it will still be collected according to the original tax rate, plus a penalty.

The silk industry is on the verge of bankruptcy.

The Five Silk Mills Suspend Operations Again

Stabilizing Silk Prices is Underway

Representatives from the Ministry of Industry Will Arrive in Shanghai Shortly

The Ta Kung Pao reports that of the silk mills in Shanghai that are barely managing to operate, only thirty-three remain. Due to substantial losses, they are unable to sustain operations. Following the recent closure of three mills, five more were forced to shut down yesterday, exacerbating the precarious situation. The Ta Kung Pao reporter continued to inquire from various sources, and the details are as follows:

Five More Mills Forced to Close

Recently, the Jiyu Silk Mill on Gonghe Road in Zhabei, the Yutong Silk Mill on Meiyuan Road, and the Yingfeng Silk Mill on Tanjiaqiao, all closed on the first of this month due to losses exceeding 20,000 yuan per mill within a month of operation, making it impossible to continue. Yesterday, five more mills announced their closure: Heji and Tongyi on Tiantong Road in Hongkou, Fuxing and Dechang in Zhabei, and Jingwei in the concession area. Only twenty-five mills in the city are still barely operating, and it is feared that they will also close down in the coming week. They are currently rushing to reel the remaining dry cocoons to prepare to pay off the remaining wages, it is said.

Stabilizing Silk Prices is Underway

Silk mill operators from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai previously held a joint meeting in Shanghai to seek temporary relief for the silk industry. They resolved to appoint Shen Huachen, Jiang Laixian, Qin Youhe, and others as representatives to negotiate with various parties on ways to stabilize silk prices. At that time, progress was stalled because Cai Shengbai, chairman of the Silk Weavers' Guild, was away from Shanghai on business. Yesterday, the Ta Kung Pao reporter met with Shen Huachen, chairman of the Shanghai Silk Mill Operators' Guild, who stated that he had contacted Cai Shengbai and others regarding stabilizing silk prices, and they expressed considerable sympathy. However, the matter is of great importance and requires careful planning to achieve effective results. Therefore, further consultations are needed in the coming days before a decision can be made.

Representatives from the Ministry of Industry Will Arrive in Shanghai Shortly

The Executive Yuan has instructed the Ministries of Finance and Industry to formulate four measures to aid the silk industry in Shanghai, and to implement them separately. The first measure, exempting all local taxes on silkworm cocoons and factory silk, is to be handled by the provincial and municipal governments of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Shanghai. The second measure, reducing silk cocoon transportation costs, is to be handled by the Ministries of Transportation and Railways. The third measure is to request the National Economic Council to establish a Silk Industry Control Council as soon as possible. The fourth measure, concerning fundraising or issuing public bonds, is of great importance and requires further consultation. It is reported that the Ministry of Industry, in order to expedite relief efforts, has sent Liu Yinfu, Director of the Department of Industry, to Shanghai for investigation. Mr. Liu is expected to arrive in Shanghai shortly to consult with Mayor Wu and the silk mill operators' association before making a decision, it is said.

Rice Merchants Await Foreign Rice

It is Said That the Existing Rice Reserves

Can Only Last for One Month

The price of rice in Shanghai remains high due to the worsening drought in various regions. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Jiang Shizhi, chairman of the Rice Grain Association, yesterday, who provided an overview of the grain situation, which is detailed below:

Reasons for the Price Hike

Mr. Jiang first stated that the reasons for the high rice prices in Shanghai are: (1) Wuhu's ban on rice exports; (2) Hunan's increase in grain export taxes; (3) the worsening drought in various regions; (4) high prices of flour and wheat; (5) the military headquarters purchasing 20,000 shi of indica rice, which is still ongoing. Due to these five factors, the supply has decreased, and demand has increased, leading to speculation and hoarding. Although the market price is nominally 13 yuan, the unofficial price has already reached 13.70 yuan. This month is also a period of scarcity before the new harvest, so the price surge is just gaining momentum.

Foreign Rice is Coming

He continued, saying that the banking industry and the rice industry have ordered foreign rice from Saigon. The total order amounts to 150,000 shi for the banking industry and 200,000 shi for the rice industry. 100,000 shi are expected to arrive this month, and the rest will be imported next month. Currently, the selling price in Saigon is 12 yuan. The cost of the first batch ordered by the banking and rice industries is 10.30 yuan, and the second batch is 11.40 yuan. Therefore, there is no profit to be made from the second batch. It is heard that the banking industry's rice will be hoarded in anticipation of price increases. Tongli japonica rice has already been sold for 12.40 yuan. This year, Tongli rice was originally 4 yuan cheaper than Changbang (i.e., top-grade white rice). Therefore, the current market price of 13 yuan for top-grade white rice is still considered restrained. If it were according to reason, it should be sold for 16 yuan.

Rice Reserves in Shanghai

Finally, he said that the current reserves of top-grade white rice in Shanghai total 300,000 shi. The four rice mills have a reserve of 10,000 packages, and the Xieji Company has a reserve of 8,000 packages. These are all indica, japonica, and glutinous rice, totaling over 400,000 shi for the entire city. However, this grain is not suitable for use in other areas. Assuming a daily consumption of 15,000 shi for the entire city, it can only last for one month. The foreign warehouses between Xinzhalan Bridge and Xinqiao in the new garbage bridge area still have 100,000 shi of rice held as collateral. The foreign warehouses in Pudong still have Hunan indica, Jiangxi japonica, Anhui indica, Saigon indica, and small broken rice from three years ago, totaling over 100,000 shi. If we desire stabilized rice prices, we must wait for foreign rice to arrive in Shanghai before we can expect a price drop, he said.

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Committee

Yesterday Hosted the Press

Reporting on Various Agreed Upon Measures with the Rickshaw Owners

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that after the resolution of the rickshaw dispute in the Public Concession, the Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Management Committee hosted news reporters from various newspapers at 3:00 PM yesterday to explain the benefits of the new regulations for rickshaw owners and pullers. Chairman Massey denied any passive intent and simultaneously announced the application status of new applicants, stating that there were no remaining licenses. The details are recorded below:

Massey's Report

Massey, Chairman of the Rickshaw Management Committee, met with reporters at the Shanghai Municipal Council's office on Jiangxi Road at 3:00 PM yesterday, translated by Zhu Maodeng. He said that he was very pleased with the measures agreed upon by both parties regarding new rickshaws. The mission of the Committee is to alleviate the suffering of rickshaw pullers and to promote the welfare of society, with no other intentions. As for the reports that he could not implement his personal ideas and expressed a passive attitude, he had no such intention and no reason to resign. (Note from the Xin Sheng News Agency: Massey's passive statement was rumored by the rickshaw owners, who said that Mr. Massey made this statement at the equal meeting held by the Shanghai Municipal Council on Monday.)

Mutual Aid and Relief

Regarding the Mutual Aid and Relief Association, there is a council consisting of ten directors, four foreigners and six Chinese. The licensed rickshaw owners and registered rickshaw pullers each send two representatives to supervise the use of funds. Whether to add more directors in the future will depend on the situation. The rickshaw owners have also clearly understood this mutual aid fund for rickshaw pullers and hope for cooperation from all parties. Mutual aid for rickshaw pullers is helping oneself, not charity. There are many misunderstandings about this point outside. Registered rickshaw pullers, in case of illness or accidents, can request relief from the Mutual Aid and Relief Association. Those who are not genuinely licensed rickshaw pullers cannot enjoy this right.

Registered Rickshaw Owners

Regarding the implementation of the new regulations, the reports that the Shanghai Municipal Council accepted the rickshaw owners' conditions are completely misunderstood. The Shanghai Municipal Council has not abandoned the principles of improving rickshaw designs and various other aspects. The renting, selling, and mortgaging of rickshaw licenses completely contradict the new and old regulations. A license, with a rickshaw worth 70 yuan, could be sold for 700 yuan. Those who profited without labor were all created by the rickshaw pullers working like cattle and horses. Therefore, the new regulations stipulate that only genuine rickshaw owners can obtain a license. To avoid these abuses, the deadline has been extended to the 13th. Licenses will not be issued without proof of ownership, so that rickshaw owners can truly benefit. Those concerned about the reform of rickshaws can contribute their questions or opinions to the Committee as much as possible. The Committee will not hold any prejudice.

Rickshaw Rental Standard

After the new regulations were resolved in a bilateral meeting, the daily rickshaw rental is 7 jiao and 8 fen of silver dollars, plus 7 fen for the mutual aid fund. In addition, rickshaw owners must pay 1.50 yuan per month for the mutual aid fund. The rickshaw pullers have also expressed to the Shanghai Municipal Council's Rickshaw Affairs Committee that they are still paying an excess of 1 jiao and 1 fen of small dollars per day and requested a reduction. Due to the fluctuating price of silver dollars, this amount was set at the request of the rickshaw owners. The 10 jiao of small dollars set by the research association last year is equivalent to 7 jiao and 8 fen of silver dollars. Therefore, to ensure that neither party suffers a loss, it was set as silver dollars. As for the 40,000 registered rickshaw pullers, outsiders do not understand and say that there are over 100,000 rickshaw pullers, which is not enough. This is a misunderstanding. If a rickshaw puller returns to his hometown, the licensed rickshaw pullers, if there are not enough, can apply to the Committee for a license at any time, without worry.

New Rickshaw Style

As for the improved new rickshaw style, seven new styles have been submitted and are being inspected at the Transport Office, with economy, durability, and aesthetics as the criteria. A decision will be made in about two weeks. The rumor that all rickshaws in the city must be replaced after the new rickshaw style is approved is a misunderstanding. Existing rickshaws must be inspected by the Shanghai Municipal Council's Transport Office after two months. If the inspection reveals that they are old and dilapidated or the rickshaw body is not sturdy, they must be eliminated and replaced with new rickshaws. If the entire city were to be completely replaced, it would take several years to be uniform. Therefore, the rickshaw owners should not view it as a difficult problem.

Started Receiving Licenses Yesterday

The Rickshaw Affairs Committee Notified Newly Registered Rickshaw Owners Yesterday

The Old Rickshaw Owners Have Complied with the Regulations and There Are No Remaining Licenses

After the resolution of the rickshaw problem in the Public Concession, the rickshaw owners in the Special District started receiving licenses yesterday. Old Rickshaw Owners Receiving Licenses

The rickshaw owners who have received the lower part of the form took it to the Committee yesterday morning to exchange it for a rickshaw owner's certificate, and then went to the Donation Office and Transport Office to pay the donation and receive the business license for August. New Rickshaw Owners Eliminated

A large number of people applied at that time. Now, because the old rickshaw owners are willing to comply with the Council's regulations, and the Council has extended the deadline for issuing rickshaw owner's certificates to allow them to do so, it is feared that there will be no remaining licenses to give to the new applicants. The Committee has now notified the applicants of this situation.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council

Questioning the Reason for Increased House Tax

Arbitrarily Increasing the Original House Tax Contradicts the Regulations

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council yesterday, which reads: Respectfully, according to a letter from taxpayer Fan Xiaoling, regarding the illegal and unreasonable increase in house tax by the Donation Office of the Shanghai Municipal Council: I, Fan Xiaoling, rent a three-story building at No. 10, Lane 397, Jiujiang Road. The front door is inside the lane, and the back door faces Jiujiang Road. The monthly rent is 176.22 yuan, and the quarterly house tax is 73.50 yuan. Recently, the three tenants in the downstairs wing rooms and back shed of the rented building, due to sluggish business, wanted to maintain their business and facilitate customer access. They asked me to obtain the landlord's permission to open a doorway in the wall of the back shed facing the road. This was entirely intended to help them make a living, and the rent for the three tenants was not increased by a single cent. However, the Donation Office saw this as an opportunity to make money and suddenly increased the house tax by 21 yuan this quarter, to 94.50 yuan. I only learned of this when paying the tax. When I inquired at the Donation Office, they said that it was because a doorway had been added, and also because an investigation revealed that my rental income and expenses were sustainable. Based on a unilateral assumption, they concluded that the profit margin was high. Furthermore, they claimed that house tax is not based on rent. Calculating house tax based on the amount of rent has always been the established rule in the Public Concession and needs no further explanation. Even if the Donation Office has disregarded the established rules of the Shanghai Municipal Council and arbitrarily changed its common practice, there should still be a standard to follow when calculating house tax. If the rent of the building is used as a standard for types such as shops or residences, then, for example, if there are four buildings of the same size and with the same rent, one is rented to a bank, one is used as a shop, one has a store name, and one is a residence, will the house tax be divided into four different levels? Furthermore, if there are two equal buildings, one has one-third used as a shop and the rest as a residence, and the other has two-thirds used as a shop and the rest as a residence, what is the standard? If it is said that it does not depend on the size of the location but on the capital and business situation, then there are differences such as small shops with large capital, large shops with small capital, businesses with little capital but wide reach, and businesses with much capital but narrow reach. This means that the Donation Office will also be responsible for checking the account books of all shops in the district. As for the amount of rental income, the Donation Office has no right to use it as an excuse. If the Donation Office believes that a tenant's income can offset expenses and thus increase the tax, then if the rental income is not enough to cover expenses, will the Donation Office be considerate enough to exempt or reduce the tax and provide additional subsidies to make up the difference? In addition to the monthly rent, the tenant must also bear the burden of house tax, electricity bill, doorman fee, repair fee, vacant rooms, the loss of rent owed by the three tenants, the depreciation of small rents and electricity meters, and the mental trouble, etc. The rental income of my building and all expenses are losing a lot. So is the Donation Office's tax rate based on the number of doors of the building? I am confused and unclear. I respectfully submit this request, hoping that you will forward it to the Donation Office of the Shanghai Municipal Council and quickly change the arbitrarily increased amount of 94.50 yuan back to 73.50 yuan, so that I can pay the tax according to the regulations and fulfill the reasonable obligation of a resident taxpayer. Otherwise, before I receive a fair resolution, I can only temporarily deposit the unpaid amount of 73.50 yuan in the bank to clarify that the responsibility for the delay is not mine, etc., and submit an income and expense statement to the Association. After investigating the points mentioned in the letter, this Association believes that they are reasonable. With the actual amount of rent and the total donation, there should be no problem at all. If the aim is to increase revenue due to insufficient tax collection, instead of coming up with various reasons to squeeze the remaining shops, making it impossible for them to survive, why not implement the resolution of the Taxpayer Representative Assembly and collect taxes on vacant rooms, which would not contradict the regulations? As for the income and expense statement, there is no obligation to report it, but in order for your office to understand the financial situation of the taxpayer regarding rent, it is enclosed for your reference.

One Freight Car No. 4001

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning and Was Detained for Inspection

The Medicinal Herbs Inside Emitted an Opium-Like Odor

It Was Only After Finding No Illegal Items That They Realized It Was a Misunderstanding

The Xin Sheng News Agency reports that the Shanghai-Beiping Joint Transport freight car No. 4001, which departed from Beiping, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. The Garrison Headquarters and the Municipal Government ordered the detention and inspection of a freight car containing medicinal herbs. However, no illegal items were found. The details are recorded below:

Opium Odor

When the road protection soldiers inspected freight car No. 45280, a 40-ton car, on the Jinpu Railway's Pukou Station before noon, an opium-like odor was emitted. The stationmaster was asked to open the door for inspection, but the station claimed that freight transported jointly could not be inspected en route. After arriving at the capital, the soldiers placed a seal on the car that read "Sealed by the soldiers of the Jinghu-Huhangyong Road Protection Soldier Detachment of the Soldier Headquarters, July 7." It was found that July was actually a mistake and should have been August.

Telegraph to Shanghai to Detain

The soldier detachment, in addition to reporting to the capital's Soldier Headquarters to telegraph Shanghai to inspect the car upon arrival, also sent soldiers to accompany the car to Shanghai. The Shanghai Municipal Government and the Garrison Headquarters received a telegram from the capital's Soldier Headquarters stating that one of the freight cars containing medicinal herbs on the Shanghai-Beiping Joint Transport freight car No. 4001 emitted an opium-like odor when passing through Pukou. They were asked to inspect it upon arrival in Shanghai. They immediately dispatched soldiers and police to the Maigen Road freight station yesterday morning, together with the railway police from both railways. When the car arrived at the station, it was unloaded, and the suspicious car was driven directly to the North Station and stopped on track No. 1.

Inspection Results

The Garrison Headquarters sent soldiers, together with police from the Public Security Bureau and railway police from both railways, one person each, to guard the car. At 12:00 noon, together with the freight owner, they opened the door for inspection on the spot. All the goods were opened, and the boxes and packages were thoroughly inspected. The inspection was completed at 2:00 PM. As a result, no illegal items were found. The medicinal herbs that emitted the opium-like odor, totaling 32 items, were all Chinese medicines such as codonopsis pilosula and honeysuckle. Due to the hot weather and moisture, they emitted an odor similar to opium, leading to a misunderstanding. Now, the goods have been either taken away by the freight owner or put into storage. The empty car has been attached to the Shanghai-Beiping freight car No. 4002 heading north.

National Artists

Preparing to Establish a Productive Arts Society

Using Science to Innovate China's Industrial Production

To Fuse Inherent Art with Modern Life

The art community in Shanghai has recently initiated the formation of a "Productive Arts Research Society," a joint organization of the national art and craft community. The list of founders includes Teng Gu (Nanjing), Dong Shouping (Shanxi), Chu Xiaoshi (Beiping), Zhou Xibao (Hangzhou), Yu Shujun (pattern designer), Lin Jianfeng (Nanyang), Qian Jiuding, Zhou Zugao, Teng Baiye (Shanghai), and others. Since the society's planning and preparation over the past month, it has established standards for the advocacy of artistic production and is scheduled to be established on the 15th of this month. Excerpts from its main advocacy and planning outline are as follows:

Artistic Production Advocacy The Society advocates (1) the production of art, (2) the artification of life, and (3) the integration of China's inherent productive art with modern life. China's current weakness, economic crisis, and cultural decline are related to the degradation and backwardness of Chinese art. The reasons are obvious, and the urgent way to save the situation, besides the three principles mentioned above, there is really no other way. However, how these principles can be achieved, all depend on the Society's proposal. The state should establish an Art Guidance Bureau before implementing various plans.

Artistic Production Plan The planned artistic production plans to be promoted are (1) the construction of artistic production schools, (2) industrial and commercial art guidance, (3) urban art construction, (4) international art promotion, A. Overseas art exhibitions, B. Overseas art lecture tours, (5) public art education, A. Improvement of drama, film, and songs, B. Establishment of museums, C. Public art lectures, D. Children's art education facilities

Plans to Establish a Production School In addition, after the establishment of the Society, it plans to run an art and craft production school. The main outline of the plan is (1) the organization of the art and craft production school, which includes the following three main parts: A. University Department, B. Vocational Department, C. Social Department. (2) The University Department aims to preserve the national essence, promote China's inherent arts and crafts, use Western physical and chemical sciences to innovate China's industrial production, advocate and study social productionism, and promote China's Renaissance as the biggest lecturing goal. (3) The Vocational Department is responsible for implementing vocational education in arts and crafts, cultivating specialized talents for China's new artistic and craft production. (4) The Social Department aims to serve and guide the entire society's craft production, and has various instructors to be prepared for various requests for guidance and learning. (5) The organization of the University Department is as follows: A. Painting Department, research and practice of the history, theory, and learning of Chinese and Western painting. B. Chemistry Department, researching and manufacturing various pigments, artificial stones, electroplating, and other crafts, and researching organic chemistry. C. Music Department, research on music, drama, and film. D. Applied Arts Institute, the Applied Arts Institute is divided into the following three departments: 1. Architecture Department, architectural composition of buildings, boats, cars, airplanes, etc. 2. Sculpture Department, architectural sculpture, human sculpture, applied sculpture, such as (wood, bamboo, copper, jade, etc. sculpture). 3. Pattern Department, interior decoration design, clothing design, furniture design, textile pattern design, silk carpet and carpet design, wallpaper, advertising painting, toy, miscellaneous design, etc. (6) The organization of the Vocational Department is as follows: A. Earthwork, ceramics, glass, cement, artificial stone, toys, etc. manufacturing. B. Carpentry, house, tables and chairs, boats, cars, boxes, etc. manufacturing and wood carving. C. Metalwork, jewelry, copper turning, iron turning, sculpture, shadow cloisonné, and the manufacture of various metal tools. D. Dyeing and weaving, weaving cloth, weaving silk, weaving velvet, dyeing, bleaching, washing, and dyeing, and researching methods. E. Chemical industry, papermaking, leather making, rubber, cement, artificial stone, photographic materials, miscellaneous toys, etc. manufacturing. (7) Social Department, the organization and work of the Social Department should go deep into the people. Provinces, cities, counties, and districts all have branches. According to the size and situation of the region, several professors are hired to be prepared for social inquiries. Regardless of factories, shops, private families, all have the right to gather comrades, apply for reasons, and request guidance on any simple daily craft methods and theories. The subjects are A. Knotting velvet, B. Embroidery, C. Home hygiene, D. Childcare knowledge, E. Scientific knowledge, F. Cooking, G. Interior decoration, H. Tailoring, I. Clothing pattern, J. Carpentry knowledge, K. Electrical knowledge, L. Economic knowledge.

Shanghai County News Yesterday

Inauguration Ceremony of Minxin Building

Former Mingxin Temple Bronze Bell Renamed Rest Bell

Three-Story Building on the West Side of Hu Min Road, North Bridge

According to the Xinsheng Society, all sectors of Shanghai County, in order to preserve antiquities, have specially renovated the Mingxin Temple bell tower into the Minxin Building, and held an inauguration ceremony at the North Bridge County Government yesterday. Details are as follows:

Attendees included Shanghai County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia, Standing Committee Member of the County Party Department Zhang Jingye, Chief of the County Public Security Bureau Xu Minyin, Chief of the County Education Bureau Zhu Changlin, Huang Yunzhen of the County Property Committee, Yin Shisheng of the Shangsong Automobile Company, Lu Bohong of the China Merchants Electric Tram Company, and representatives from various county-level agencies and organizations such as Cao Jifu, Cha Housheng, and more than a hundred others. The meeting was chaired by Pan Zhongjia, with Cao Jifu as the recorder and Xu Yamin as the master of ceremonies.

Ceremony Order: (1) Everyone stands at attention; (2) Sing the Party song; (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and National Flag and the portrait of the Premier; (4) The chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will; (5) Silent tribute; (6) Report; (7) Speech; (8) Unveiling; (9) Photography; (10) Ceremony concludes.

After the chairman reported that the meeting commenced and saluted as required, Chairman Pan Zhongjia reported: Today is the opening day of the Minxin Building, which has been renovated by our county. I am very honored that everyone has come from afar. It is a pity that the wind and rain have caused some regrets to this grand ceremony. Regarding the reconstruction of the Mingxin Temple, everyone should be aware that when the restoration was initiated in the winter of the 20th year of the Republic, it went through several twists and turns before construction could begin in June last year. It was completed on May 2nd of this year. It was originally planned to be unveiled earlier, but because this is the only achievement of North Bridge, a meeting was convened in Shanghai to propose management methods and utilization methods, and a committee was established, which delayed the unveiling until today. All expenses were purely donated by local communities in the county, totaling more than 7,000 yuan. According to the construction contract, there are still several hundred yuan remaining. Considering that what is lacking here is beverages, I plan to use the remaining amount to build a self-flowing well. From the winter of the 20th year, until now, two and a half years, I thank all sectors for their spiritual and material assistance. I, on behalf of Shanghai County, express my gratitude to everyone.

Representative speeches were followed by Zhang Jingye, Yin Shisheng and others reporting the brief history of the Minxin Building: According to the Mingxin Temple records, the bell tower was first built in the summer of the 17th year of Song Ningzong (Jiashen year), initially with an iron bell. In the 33rd year of Ming Jiajing (Jiayin year), it was abandoned due to Japanese pirate disturbances. It was rebuilt in the 14th year of Wanli (Bingxu year), and a large bronze bell was cast, which is the ancient bell preserved today. The bell is six feet tall, five feet in diameter, and engraved with inscriptions of the Ming Minister of Rites Lu Shusheng's assistance, with donor inscriptions and the names of benevolent men and women. In the sixth year of Chongzhen (Guiyou year), in June, it was destroyed by a hurricane. It was rebuilt in the sixteenth year. During the Kangxi and Qianlong periods of the Qing Dynasty, it was repaired twice. Since the tenth year of Qianlong, it has been in disrepair for a long time. On September 2, in the 22nd year of the Republic, when a hurricane passed, the entire building collapsed at noon, and the pillars and stones were dismantled. Only the bell remained unscathed. Previously, in the winter of the 21st year of the Republic, local figures requested the county magistrate to gather celebrities to initiate fundraising for restoration, and a committee was organized with separate economic and engineering departments in charge of the matter. From January of the 21st year to March of the 22nd year, more than 5,730 yuan was collected in donations from public groups and private individuals. In June of the 22nd year, the county government invited bids for construction, shifting the foundation northward, about a hundred steps from the original site. Construction began in June and was completed in May of the following year. After the completion and acceptance of the work, the county government convened a meeting to discuss internal facilities management methods, naming it Minxin, and decided to hang the bell on the top floor for rest and general notification. The middle floor is used as a library, and the lower floor is used as an exhibition hall, for the public to visit and read. It is not only for the preservation of antiquities.

Guided Tour: Magistrate Pan then led the crowd to the front of the building's gate, unveiled it, and entered. The building is 17.98 meters high, the platform is 15.53 meters wide, and the four sides are 8.83 meters wide. It is located on the west side of the Hu-Min Motor Road and is divided into three floors. The ground floor displays agricultural products, the second floor is a library, and the thousand-jin giant bell is hung in the center of the third floor, named the Rest Bell. The walls are inscribed by Wang Yiting and others with the characters "Bell Tower," "Thought-Provoking," "Clear Sounds Reach the Roots," and "A Hundred and Eight Together Reflect." Ascending the tower for a distant view, the scenery is picturesque. The tour ended at 5:00 PM, and everyone dispersed.

Japanese Residents

Satisfied with Rent Reduction

Landlords Appease Foreigners

Why Do They Treat Our Compatriots This Way?

According to the Japanese-language Shanghai Daily News yesterday, the Rent Reduction Committee held a meeting at the United Association Office on the 8th. The committee members reported on the progress of the rent reduction movement and discussed how to prevent landlords from raising rents again in the future. At the same time, they were satisfied that most landlords on North Sichuan Road have automatically reduced rents, so the Rent Reduction Movement Committee will be disbanded soon. It is now found that the implemented reductions are: Shigaota Road Mainland Lane reduced by 20%, Huayuan Lane 18.85%, Dongzhao Lane 15% to 20%, McNear Lane 15%, the Kabukai-za area 15%, and the Japanese Autonomous Association section of the houses owned by the Li and Yang families reduced by 12.5% to 20%. Also, places like Shigaota Road Qianai Lane, Fengle Lane, Arui Lane, Xuqing Lane, and Yong'an Lane generally agreed to reduce by 15%. Therefore, the Japanese Residents Committee believes that the goal has been achieved, and the movement has come to an end. The United Association Committee does not need to exist.

This shows that there is a growing need for communication between Chinese and foreign cultures, and since languages are different, drama is the only way to understand each other. Li Shilin Mourns His Wife's Death After Childbirth

Sues Women's Hospital Director and Doctor

Second Special Court Holds Trial Yesterday, Medical Community Attends to Observe

Li Describes in Detail His Wife's Admission to the Hospital and Tragic Death

丨The court orders to summon Dr. Chen Jingxu for further questioning丨

Li Shilin, a local residing at No. 34 Shangxian Lane, Route de Saulnier in the French Concession and opening the Donghua Engineering and Construction Company on Beijing Road, is forty years old this year. His wife, Wang, is about thirty-five or six years old, and the couple has a deep affection for each other. They have already had six children, and she recently became pregnant again, for her seventh childbirth. On June 29 of this year, when her pregnancy reached full term, she felt pain in her abdomen in the morning and was about to give birth. Li immediately sent her to Shangxian Hall Women and Children's Obstetrics Hospital at No. 1 Route de Saulnier behind Shangxian Lane to await delivery. At 10:00 AM that morning, she gave birth to a son, delivered by Dr. Ge Chenghui. Mother and child were safe at the time of delivery. Unexpectedly, three days later, the parturient suddenly became ill, with a fever rising to over 100 degrees. Because there was no proper treatment in the hospital, Li took her home and sought medical treatment on his own.

Treatment Ineffective

She died on July 12. Li Shilin believed that his wife's illness and death were due to the hospital's disregard for patients, negligence of duty, and failure to provide medical treatment. He was heartbroken and hired Yan Yinwu and Lu Congzu as lawyers to file a complaint with the Second Special District Court, based on Article 291 of the Criminal Law, suing Zhang Xiangwen, director of Shangxian Hall Women and Children's Hospital, Dr. Ge Chenghui, head nurse Gu Qin, and others for negligence of duty resulting in death, requesting that they be summoned and punished according to law. Upon receiving the complaint, the court specially opened the second criminal court yesterday morning, presided over by Criminal Court President Wang Gangxu, to summon both parties for trial. The plaintiff and lawyers Yan and Lu arrived at the court, and the defendants and their defense lawyer Tan Yigong also arrived. The audience in the gallery

Mostly Women

Especially those from the medical community. After the court opened, the judge first asked both parties about their age, origin, occupation, and address. Then, the plaintiff, Li Shilin, stated the facts of the complaint: My wife, Wang, was pregnant at full term and felt abdominal pain on the morning of June 29 of this year. I immediately accompanied her to Shangxian Hall Women and Children's Obstetrics Hospital, staying in a first-class room to await delivery. She was delivered by Dr. Ge Chenghui, and at 10:05 AM that morning, she gave birth to a boy. The parturient had previously given birth safely six times, and I always wanted to hire a midwife to deliver her. This time, she was sent to the hospital for delivery, especially because the time was ripe, without any obstacles or symptoms of illness. She was also very safe after delivery. On June 30, for some reason, the hospital director, Zhang Xiangwen, asked a Dr. Huang to conduct an examination on her behalf. On July 1, the parturient suddenly developed a fever. Logically, the doctor should

Fever in the Body

Carefully and meticulously examine the cause of the fever and treat it properly. However, the defendants did not pay attention and only said that it was milk engorgement, and that she only needed to drink less boiled water and eat less porridge to reduce the fever, without providing appropriate treatment. As a result, the fever rose even higher the next day. At that time, the parturient was very afraid of the cold and felt uneasy. She asked the doctor to see the fever chart herself, but the hospital refused to let her see it, only saying that she had a slight fever and that there was no problem, as long as she rested quietly for three days. In the afternoon, I went to visit and brought my own thermometer. I suddenly saw that the parturient's fever had risen to 104.2 degrees Fahrenheit. The room smelled terrible. I was shocked and looked around the room, but there was no one to take care of her. I hurriedly pressed the electric bell and asked a nurse to come and ask a doctor to come for examination. However, after waiting for a long time, no one entered the room. I went to the nurse's room on the second floor of the hospital, but the head nurse and nurses

No One Inside

This shows the hospital's neglect of patients, beyond compare. On the afternoon of July 4, I asked Dr. Chen Jingxu to go for a consultation. As soon as he entered the ward, he smelled a strange odor. Dr. Chen said that it was probably puerperal fever. Upon closer inspection, the parturient's body was covered with red and white spots, and the fever was as high as 104.8 degrees. It was indeed puerperal fever, caused by incomplete surgery during childbirth and careless disinfection and postpartum care. I knew the illness was critical and that it was useless to stay in the hospital, so I decided to move her back home and seek medical treatment elsewhere. However, the hospital forced her to sign a pre-printed voluntary discharge form, which was extremely hateful. After the parturient was carried home, Drs. Chen and Diao Xinde both diagnosed that it was

Puerperal Fever

And gave her injections for treatment, but it was difficult to save her. At 2:30 AM on the night of July 12, she died. Before her death, the parturient loudly complained that her life was completely lost at the hands of the hospital. Therefore, I hate the hospital's negligence and harm to human life, and I request the court to strictly investigate and punish the defendants for their due crimes. The official interrogated the defendant Zhang Xiangwen, who stated that the plaintiff's wife, Li Wang, came to the hospital for delivery, delivered by Dr. Ge. After delivery, Dr. Ge resigned on July 1 and left. After she left, I hired Drs. Hu Yizhu, Kuang Cuie, and Wang Baozhen to take turns to treat her. From July 1, Li Wang was seen by Dr. Hu and others. On July 1, Li Wang suddenly developed a fever of 101 degrees, which subsided. On the 2nd, it rose to over 101 degrees again. At that time, everyone

Thought it Was Milk Engorgement

And gave her milk-reducing medicine. On the afternoon of July 3, Dr. Hu examined Li Wang's white blood cells and found them to be over 8,000, which did not seem to indicate puerperal fever. On the afternoon of July 4, the plaintiff requested to take her back, and we did not stop him. Ge Chenghui stated that I only delivered the baby and resigned after delivery. Before I left, Li Wang showed no signs of illness. Gu Qin stated that I am the head nurse and am not in charge of what medicine the patient takes. The daily diagnosis was made by Dr. Hu and others. The court also summoned witnesses Tan Suzhen and others for questioning. The official stated that the case still requires summoning witness Dr. Chen Jingxu and others, and ordered them to adjourn the court and wait for a scheduled summons for further questioning, and then adjourned the court.

Murderer Zhu Gengshan's Followers are Numerous, So the Trial is Transferred to Shanghai

The Debate Has Ended Yesterday and Sentencing is Scheduled for the 14th of This Month

In Huangjia Road Town, Nanhui County, on June 7 of this year, Tang Yinlou teased a female worker at a sock factory. Yang Qiusheng saw this and rebuked him. Tang sued Zhu Gengshan (also known as Zhu Xiaomao, an unemployed Shandong native), Chen Yirong (currently a police officer, Anhui native), Hu Yaohai (a worker, Hebei native), Zhang Zhenjiang (a coppersmith, Nanhui native), Wang Shoushan (an unemployed Shandong native), Zhang Zhongyi (a lantern maker, Ningbo native), and others, gathered many people, and went to the town to seek revenge and riot. The whole town was shocked. Jiang Jinsong, a clerk at the First District Office of the county, went to investigate. Zhu Gengshan, Hu Yaohai, and others believed that he was obstructing them, so they stabbed Jiang Jinsong and Zhu Azhang and Ni Alou who were beside him with knives. Zhu Gengshan even dared to hold a box cannon in his hand and show it to the crowd. Fortunately, he was seized by merchant Zhu Guoxiang. At the same time, Zhu Gengshan was also beaten by Jiang Jinsong, Yang Yunchu, Yang Miaosheng, Yang Gensheng, Yang Qiusheng, Jiang Yezi, Zhu Azhang, and others. At that time, the situation was quite violent. All the shops in the town, seeing the large number of people and holding military weapons and bayonets, suspected that they were huge bandits looting, so they closed their doors and went on strike. County Magistrate Yuan of Nanhui not only detained Zhu Gengshan and others, but also found that Zhu Gengshan's followers who carried weapons to commit crimes were extremely numerous, and there were also many police officers in active service under his command. The government, in hearing this case, was deeply afraid that other accidents would occur and endanger public security. Therefore, it applied to the Jiangsu Higher Court to transfer jurisdiction. The Higher Court designated the Shanghai Local Court to handle the case. On one hand, the Nanhui County Government escorted Zhu Gengshan, Chen Yirong, Hu Yaohai, Zhang Zhenjiang, Wang Shoushan, Zhang Zhongyi, and others in custody to the Local Court for detention pending instructions. On the other hand, Jiang Jinsong, Yang Yunchu, Yang Miaosheng, Yang Gensheng, Yang Qiusheng, Jiang Yezi, and Zhu Azhang, who were released on bail, were ordered to surrender themselves to the court for interrogation. Now it is known that Prosecutor Xiao Jinrong has completed the investigation of the defendants for obstructing official duties, gathering crowds to fight, and illegally possessing firearms, and has filed a public prosecution. Zhu Gengshan was accused of holding a gun to gather a crowd, and Hu Yaohai was accused of beating Jiang Jinsong. Zhu Gengshan was also accused of injuring Zhu Azhang and Ni Alou. The First District Office clerk Jiang Jinsong went to investigate Zhu Gengshan, Chen Yirong, Hu Yaohai, Zhang Zhenjiang, Wang Shoushan, and Zhang Zhongyi, and implemented violent coercion. Jiang Jinsong, Yang Yunchu, Yang Miaosheng, Yang Gensheng, Jiang Yezi, Yang Qiusheng, and Zhu Azhang were also accused of jointly injuring Zhu Gengshan. All of these facts were clear. Zhu Gengshan, Chen Yirong, Hu Yaohai, Zhang Zhenjiang, Wang Shoushan, and Zhang Zhongyi were jointly accused of violating Article 142, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. Zhu Gengshan and Hu Yaohai were also accused of violating Article 293, Paragraph 1 of the same law. Zhu Gengshan was also accused of violating Article 1, Paragraph 1 of the Military Firearms Control Regulations for possessing military firearms for criminal purposes. Jiang Jinsong, Yang Yunchu, Yang Miaosheng, Yang Gensheng, Jiang Yezi, Yang Qiusheng, and Zhu Azhang were also accused of jointly injuring Zhu Gengshan, violating Article 293, Paragraph 1 of the same law. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun Jikang specially opened the Third Court for trial. The seven defendants, Jiang Jinsong, Yang Yunchu, and others, who were released on bail, jointly hired lawyer Pan Zhensheng to appear in court to defend them. After the judge took the stand, he ordered the six defendants in custody, Zhu Gengshan, Chen Yirong, Hu Yaohai, Zhang Zhenjiang, Wang Shoushan, and Zhang Zhongyi, and the seven defendants, Jiang Jinsong, etc., to be brought to the case for interrogation one by one. Their confessions denied the assault. The judge then asked Prosecutor Xiao to come to court to present his views. Finally, lawyer Pan Zhensheng stood up to defend them for a long time. The judge deemed the debate to be concluded and scheduled the sentencing for the 14th of this month. The six defendants, Zhu Gengshan and others, were returned to custody. The seven defendants, Jiang Jinsong and others, were released on their original bail. Then, the court adjourned.

Page 13

Public Works Bureau Discussion

Public Transportation Problems

Consider Tram Cooperation with Buses

Extend Existing Routes and Improve Equipment

丨First Consult with Neighboring Municipal Authorities丨

A memorandum regarding public transportation in the International Settlement, submitted by the Commissioner of Public Works of the Shanghai Municipal Council, was presented for discussion at the last meeting of the Public Utilities Committee. The minutes of the meeting have been approved by the Board of Directors. The scope of the Commissioner of Public Works' memorandum is quite broad, and some points seem more appropriately considered traffic issues. These should be reviewed by the Traffic Committee. Therefore, the Public Utilities Committee's discussion is limited to public transportation issues concerning the tram and bus companies.

Improving Tram Problems Regarding the improvement of trams, the Commissioner of Public Works believes that since the Shanghai Municipal Council has not indicated whether it intends to acquire the tram business in 1940, the tram company may be unwilling to undertake large capital expenditures at this time. The tram franchise agreement is perpetual, but at the end of the 35th year (i.e., 1940) or every seven years thereafter, the Shanghai Municipal Council may, with six months' prior notice, acquire the developed business. The purchase price will be the fair market value as determined by arbitration, but no compensation will be given in addition to the purchase price due to compulsory acquisition or the company's established business reputation. The Commissioner of Public Works believes that how to improve the trams should be decided first. The rail system has been abandoned by many cities, but in the case of Shanghai, it would be difficult to abolish the trams and replace them with more satisfactory alternatives.

Construction of Elevated Railways The idea of constructing elevated railways has been proposed from time to time. The Commissioner of Public Works has studied this proposal in detail and concluded that it would be difficult to implement this public transportation method solely within the International Settlement. Furthermore, the current elevated railways have a drawback: most passengers must disembark at a limited number of locations, further congesting traffic.

Abolishing Trams The Commissioner of Public Works' memorandum proposes abolishing trams and replacing them with double-decker trolleybuses, stating that adding trolleybus routes and connecting them with existing trolleybus routes is easier than connecting them with tram routes. A committee member asked where trolleybuses are slower than double-decker buses. The Commissioner replied that the cost of operating trolleybuses is cheaper than operating petroleum-powered vehicles.

Detailed Discussion Results (1) All committee members agreed that the tram company and the bus company should cooperate with each other instead of competing, and believed that this matter should be handled through consultations between the authorities of the three districts. (2) During the discussion, it was suggested that the Shanghai Municipal Council should find ways to cooperate with the French Concession and the Shanghai Municipal Government to agree on a common approach to necessary improvements in public transport services. Currently, there is a great lack of transportation links between the three districts, but the Commissioner of Public Works believes that if the municipal authorities of the three districts can openly discuss their difficulties, they may be able to develop a valuable strategy. The north-south transportation routes traversing the International Settlement are now almost entirely within the central district, and urgently need to be extended to the western district. The lack of connection and cooperation between the current tram and trolleybus routes is also a drawback. If the tram tracks on the Bund are moved closer to the river, the Garden Bridge could be rebuilt and widened to 80 feet. The Commissioner does not agree with converting the current trams into double-decker ones because all the tracks are too narrow. Trolleybuses, because they can stop on the side of the road, are convenient for traffic. However, because of rickshaws, they cannot run close to the side of the road. Trolleybuses that run on overhead wires have a drawback: their movement is restricted by the wires, so they cannot overtake each other when running, as buses can. (3) All committee members agreed that the Shanghai Municipal Council should make preliminary consultations with the municipal authorities of the Chinese and French Concessions regarding improving public transport convenience, and should also inquire with the tram company about its preparations for improving equipment. (4) All committee members also believed that extending existing routes is as important as improving equipment, but the issue of extending routes can only be considered based on the outcome of consultations with the municipal authorities of the two neighboring concessions.

Chief Culprit Arrested at Dadong Hotel

Song Bingzheng, a Chinese detective from the Criminal Investigation Division of the Central Police Station, and detectives Chen Yonggui and Xu Guirong, learned that Wang Guitong (also known as Peng Guitong), from Hunan, specialized in selling opium substitutes, white pills (also known as "quick highs"). School Principal

Joint Theft and Trafficking of Stolen Goods

Stealing Needles from Singer Company

Principal on the Run Arrested at Store

Chen Ruxin, a 20-year-old from Baoshan, the principal of the Wanguo Commercial School at No. 15 Yuxiang Lane, Qianjiatang, Avenue Joffre, was friends with Feng Xiqing, a Tianjin native who worked at the Singer Company's store. They colluded with each other, with Feng continuously stealing sewing machine needles from the company and handing them over to Chen for private sale, sharing the profits. The company was initially unaware. Recently, an employee of the company saw sewing machine needles being sold in a store on his way home from watching a movie at the Cathay Theatre. The style and trademark were exactly the same as those sold by Singer. The employee then entered the store to inquire about the price, and was told that each dozen sold for one yuan and two fen. The employee knew that only Singer sold this type of needle and that each dozen cost one yuan and five jiao. He suspected that the store was selling counterfeit goods or that the source was questionable. He reported this to the company that day, and while the company was conducting a secret investigation, Feng Xiqing suddenly left without saying goodbye. The company suspected that Feng was involved and reported it to the Central Police Station. Detective Jiang Shangpei searched Feng's room and found letters between Feng and Chen Ruxin, as well as a photo of Chen and a contract they signed for Chen to sell the stolen goods and share the profits. It was also determined that more than 1,500 dozen of these sewing machine needles had been stolen since January of this year. The day before yesterday, Detective Jiang rushed to the Wanguo Commercial School to investigate Chen. Chen tried to deny it, claiming that his surname was Wang and that he was not Chen. Detective Jiang showed him the photo, saying that his true identity could not be concealed. Chen then admitted everything and was arrested. It is unknown where Feng has fled. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special Court. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu filed a public prosecution on charges of joint theft. After Judge Zhan Liangce questioned him, he ruled that the case still needed to be investigated and adjourned the hearing for seven days. The defendant Chen Ruxin was taken back to the police station for detention. For a school principal to commit joint theft and be responsible for selling stolen goods is truly a case of greed blinding his judgment.

Electrical Engineering Expert

Zhang Yougu Returned to China Yesterday

Dr. Zhang Yougu, who graduated from the Department of Electrical Engineering of Shanghai Jiaotong University, went to study in the United States at his own expense in 1927 and entered the Massachusetts Institute of Technology, specializing in electrical engineering. He obtained a bachelor's degree in 1929 and then interned at the General Electric Manufacturing Plant. The following year, he transferred to the Harvard University Graduate School to study radio science and obtained a doctorate. He returned to China yesterday on the Dollar Company's President Grant. Those who came to greet him at the port included his younger brother Lian Gu, his older sisters Qi Gu and Ying Gu, and relatives and friends. After seven years apart, they were finally reunited, and their emotions were extremely harmonious.
